# Task Plan: Website Perfection Pass

## Goal
Continuously reflect on and optimize the static world history timeline until it is polished, robust, historically richer, and visually coherent.

- [x] Commit and push the v315 fix.

- [x] Audit whether the current world-event layer is sufficient; use subagents for regional review and add only high-importance events.
- [x] Add an optional movable horizontal time ruler so users can align regions/entities at the same year.
- [x] Use subagent findings to add Wikipedia links inside opened detail descriptions for important entities/events, without breaking panel accessibility.
- [x] Verify static syntax, data integrity, and browser behavior after the changes.

## Quality Bar
- Runs locally without console errors.
- Timeline renders legibly on desktop and mobile.
- Core controls work: search, language, region/category filters, zoom, year jump, compare, detail panels, dark mode, full-page mode, share, export where supported.
- Layout avoids overlapping text and unstable sizing.
- Styles are consistent with the current flat cartographic design.
- Historical entity dates, labels, regions, and relationships are periodically audited against credible references.
- Visual shapes should not imply false territorial semantics: rectangular overlap is acceptable only when it means coexistence in separate columns, while partial conquest, fragmentation, or territorial contraction should have an explicit narrowing/shape language.
- Changes stay scoped and do not disturb historical data unnecessarily.

## Phases
- [x] Recover prior context and inspect repository state.
- [x] Audit current implementation and identify highest-impact issues.
- [x] Implement scoped fixes and polish.
- [x] Verify in browser across representative viewports.
- [x] Record residual risks and next opportunities.

## Decisions
- The site is static HTML/CSS/JS, so no build step is required.
- Use the existing flat, analytical design direction rather than introducing a new visual style.
- Keep planning files in the project root for ongoing work continuity.
- Use query-string asset versions for cache busting; current source references `v305`.
- Same-color adjacency is a visual border-hiding rule only; it must not merge entity IDs, hover targets, detail records, or relationship data.
- Dark mode should keep territory fills muted and dark enough to sit on the canvas, while labels remain light and readable.
- Narrow Chinese labels must not use a generic 180-degree rotation; vertical or compact labels should stay readable in normal reading direction.
- Geographic lane ordering must be checked whenever a non-contiguous owner or island lane looks displaced; Taiwan-style island owners should remain near the China coast guide rather than drifting toward unrelated mainland columns.
- On mobile, keep the header in normal document flow and collapse secondary controls behind a disclosure button.
- Detail panels should expose both visual state and accessibility state (`data-open`, `.visible`, `aria-hidden`) so focus handoff is deterministic.
- Detail panels should keep keyboard focus inside the open dialog and restore focus to the triggering timeline element on close.
- Detail panels should restore focus to the equivalent rerendered trigger when language/filter changes replace the original timeline node while the dialog is open.
- Detail panels opened from an in-panel contemporaries jump should close back to the jumped-to timeline entity rather than the older panel trigger.
- Detail panel dialogs should keep a stable `aria-labelledby` target in the DOM even while content is hidden or not yet populated.
- Compare mode should expose its chooser as a dialog with explicit open/pressed states and keyboard focus containment.
- Compare's trigger button should toggle the chooser when compare mode is not active, while `aria-pressed` remains reserved for an applied comparison.
- Compare's modal chooser should also intercept background pointer interaction with a backdrop, not only trap keyboard focus.
- Compare dialog delayed focus should be cancellable and guarded so a quick close cannot move focus into hidden options.
- Hidden dialogs should remove descendant controls from sequential focus order until the dialog is opened again.
- Dialog close paths should route through a single close routine per dialog so focus restoration, ARIA state, and descendant focusability cannot diverge.
- Export and share should fail predictably: load optional render dependencies only on demand, provide print fallback for export, and show copy failure feedback for sharing.
- Help content should remain synchronized with the current UI behavior, data counts, and dialog accessibility contract.
- Already-open dialogs should refresh localized visible text when the site language changes without losing in-progress user choices.
- Detail, world-event, and Help panels should also rerender their visible content on language changes while preserving the open dialog and recoverable in-panel focus.
- Keyboard focus on timeline blocks and event markers should provide the same preview affordance as pointer hover, while Help/README copy should state the exact activation behavior.
- Tooltip previews for activatable timeline items should include the same click and Enter/Space activation hint across polities and world-event markers.
- Shared tooltip renderers should fully overwrite or clear every visible field they own so stale metadata cannot leak between event, polity, and connection previews.
- Keyboard focus previews should temporarily connect focused timeline controls to the shared tooltip with `aria-describedby`, then remove that relationship when the preview is no longer current.
- Keyboard focus previews on polity blocks should also expose contemporaneous timeline highlights, matching the pointer hover context.
- Focus entering non-polity timeline controls should clear contemporaneous highlights, even when browser or synthetic focus sequencing does not deliver a useful block blur first.
- Non-polity timeline previews such as world-event markers and connection lines should explicitly clear polity contemporaneous highlights before showing their own tooltip.
- Tooltip placement should clamp to the viewport for all preview types so event, polity, and connection previews stay readable near screen edges.
- Timeline rerenders should clear any active tooltip preview and temporary description owner before replacing hovered or focused nodes.
- Opening modal detail/event/help panels should clear any active timeline tooltip preview before showing the dialog.
- Entering Full Page mode should clear active timeline previews before hiding surrounding UI and focusing the exit control.
- Dialog open paths that know their trigger should pass it explicitly so focus restoration does not depend on browser/programmatic click focus behavior.
- Opening the Compare modal should also clear active timeline previews and use the Compare button as the explicit restore target.
- Active timeline preview cleanup should include temporary contemporaneous highlight classes, not only tooltip UI and ARIA ownership.
- Contemporaneous hover highlighting should treat movement inside the same timeline block as internal movement, not as a preview exit.
- Pointer exit from a keyboard-focused polity block should not clear contemporaneous highlights while the focus preview is still active.
- Global Escape should route through active timeline preview cleanup so keyboard dismissal clears tooltip UI, temporary tooltip ownership, and contemporaneous highlights together.
- Mode toggles should expose pressed state and avoid leaving focus on controls hidden by the active mode.
- Share URLs should preserve Dark Mode explicitly with a `dark=1/0` flag; malformed dark-mode URL values should preserve local preference instead of forcing a mode.
- Symbolic, abbreviated, or stateful controls should expose localized accessible names and pressed/expanded state.
- Compact visual labels may be abbreviated, but the accessible names should remain complete and localized.
- URL-restored language should tolerate common English/Chinese aliases such as `zh-CN`, `zh`, `中文`, `Chinese`, `en`, and `English`, while normalizing back to the internal `cn` / `en` keys.
- Dialog trigger controls should expose expanded state only for the specific dialog content they currently own.
- Collapsible disclosure controls should wire `aria-controls`, `aria-expanded`, and content `aria-hidden` together.
- Controls inside collapsed disclosure regions should also leave the sequential focus order until the region is visible again.
- Conditionally visible controls should synchronize `hidden` state with sequential focusability instead of relying on visual hiding alone.
- Visually hidden mode-exit controls should also leave the sequential focus order while inactive.
- Full Page mode's delayed exit-button focus should be cancellable and guarded so quick exit cannot focus the hidden exit control.
- Toast notifications should let the newest message cancel any older hide timer so rapid feedback cannot disappear early.
- Global keyboard shortcuts should not operate on the background timeline while a modal dialog is open.
- Mobile pinch zoom should preserve fractional zoom steps instead of snapping to integers, and should update the URL state when the pinch ends.
- Background double-click zoom should ignore timeline controls and previewable markers so direct item interaction cannot also mutate the zoom state.
- Typography should rely on deterministic system font stacks; avoid unused external font requests and negative letter spacing.
- Chinese year labels need a wider year-scale gutter than English labels to avoid clipping on desktop and mobile.
- Every entity category present in the data should be reachable from the category filter, not only from the legend.
- Sparse category filters should move the viewport to the first visible result so a valid filter does not look empty.
- URL-restored category filters should tolerate canonical keys, English labels, Chinese labels, and surrounding whitespace while normalizing back to known category keys.
- Category filter chips should expose localized action-oriented accessible names while preserving compact visible labels.
- Stats chips should remain derived from the current rendered filter/search result and must not be overwritten by parameterless refreshes during language changes.
- Search should move the viewport to the first visible match, including when restored from a shared `search=` URL.
- URL-restored search queries should be trimmed like typed queries, so whitespace-only links recover to the default non-search state.
- Clearing search should cancel any pending debounced input query so older typed text cannot reapply after the user has cleared it.
- Zoom preset buttons should expose active/pressed state from the actual zoom value across URL load, slider changes, buttons, and keyboard shortcuts.
- URL-restored zoom values should be clamped to the same finite min/max range as runtime zoom controls.
- Share URLs should encode every reachable region-filter state, including the intentionally empty all-regions-off state.
- Malformed `regions=` URLs with no known region keys should not masquerade as the intentional all-regions-off state.
- URL-restored region and compare filters should tolerate canonical keys, full region labels, compact region labels, Chinese names, and surrounding whitespace while normalizing back to known region keys.
- Layer visibility URL flags should only accept explicit `0` / `1` values; malformed values should preserve defaults.
- Share URLs should preserve active Compare mode as a mode (`compare=`), not only as a coincidental two-region filter.
- Share URLs should preserve the current center year (`year=`) and restore it after render, while still letting search/category links auto-position when no explicit year is supplied.
- Share URLs should preserve horizontal timeline position as a normalized `x=` ratio so region-column position survives different viewport widths.
- Zoom controls should preserve the same visual timeline focus line used by `year=` sharing/restoration, not the raw viewport midpoint behind the sticky header.
- Explicit, valid URL-provided `x=` should take precedence over search/category horizontal auto-positioning during initial restoration; malformed `x=` should be ignored.
- Keyboard navigation shortcuts should synchronize `year=` and `x=` after scrolling settles so the address bar remains aligned with the actual view state.
- Viewport resize and orientation changes should preserve the current center year and horizontal timeline ratio instead of letting pixel scroll offsets drift.
- In-panel entity jumps should center the target entity both vertically and horizontally and update shareable `year=` / `x=` state.
- Manual wheel, touchpad, scrollbar, and horizontal timeline scrolling should synchronize `year=` / `x=` after scrolling settles so the visible URL reflects the actual current view.
- Language switching should preserve the current center year and horizontal timeline ratio even though Chinese mode changes the gutter/header layout.
- Region filter layout changes should preserve the current center year and horizontal timeline ratio instead of letting removed region columns push the view to a different `x=`.
- Mobile Controls expansion/collapse should preserve the current center year and horizontal timeline ratio even though header height changes substantially.
- Full Page entry/exit should preserve the current center year and horizontal timeline ratio even though the header and surrounding UI are hidden or restored.
- Timeline bottom scroll padding should be large enough for late years near AD 2000 to reach the same visual focus line as earlier years.
- Timeline top scroll padding should be large enough for early years near 3000 BC to reach the same visual focus line as later years.
- Default desktop loads without explicit view state should skip timeline edge padding so the first viewport does not look blank.
- Default mobile loads should preserve header/search/Controls context instead of auto-scrolling the header out of view.
- Mobile edge padding should be smaller than desktop edge padding while still letting explicit top-boundary links such as `year=-3000` restore correctly.
- The next data/semantics pass should inspect Hittite/Egyptian overlap as a representative case: if the shape overlap implies territorial conflict or partial conquest, the visualization needs an explicit polygon/territory-phase model rather than plain stacked rectangles.
- Optional entity fields `shape`, `territoryNote`, and `territoryNoteCN` are now the first compatibility layer for non-rectangular territory semantics; ordinary entities remain rectangular.
- Hittite/Egyptian New Kingdom data should not imply Hittites occupied Egypt. The corrected model uses Anatolian core, Egyptian Nile core, and separate half-width Levant/Syrian frontier fragments.
- Napoleonic Europe should not be rendered as one broad rectangle spanning Britain and Spain. The corrected model uses a French core, separate Italian and Rhine client/satellite fragments, and paired half-width Iberian occupation/resistance fragments.
- Hellenistic Middle East should not render Seleucid, Ptolemaic, Parthian, and Roman eastern power as mutually covering broad rectangles. The corrected model uses eastern cores, half-width Coele-Syria frontier fragments, Parthian Mesopotamian expansion, and Roman Egypt only after 30 BC.
- v121 fixed dangling historical connection endpoints: legacy `ghana`/`mali` shorthand now maps to `ghana_empire`/`mali_empire`, `dai_viet` is a real timeline entity, and Zheng He's Africa connection points to the Swahili Coast rather than Mali.
- v121 South Asia territory semantics split broad north-Indian rectangles into narrower core, Bengal, northwest, Deccan, and southern-polity fragments; sampled South Asia slot overlap is now zero.
- v121 also removed duplicate entity IDs across East Asia / Middle East / South Asia / Central Asia by adding regional suffixes for duplicate projections.
- v122 Southeast Asia semantics split Srivijaya into Sumatran core plus Malacca Strait sphere, narrowed Java/Majapahit blocks, split Sukhothai/Ayutthaya transition phases, and represented Toungoo control over Siam as a short paired fragment rather than a broad rectangle.
- v122 Africa semantics narrowed Axum, Almoravid, Almohad, Mali, Songhai, and Sokoto blocks, and separated Ife/Benin/Oyo/Ashanti into distinct Guinea Coast sub-lanes; sampled Southeast Asia and Africa slot overlap is now zero.
- v123 Americas semantics split Mesoamerica into central Mexican cores, Maya/Central America lanes, and a separate Caribbean island lane; Olmec, Teotihuacan, Toltec, and Aztec broad rectangles now use narrow influence/contact/tribute fragments beside Maya survival instead of covering it.
- v123 also splits New Spain into a Mexico-centered core plus Central American captaincy-general fragment, moves the colonial/modern Caribbean out of the Central America lane, narrows early Mexico, starts Central America at 1823, and narrows `native_nations` so it no longer covers New France/Canada.
- v124 Central Asia semantics split migration, steppe, Transoxiana, Khorasan, Afghanistan/Ghazna/Ghur, and short conquest fragments: Yuezhi now ends before the Kangju lane, Kangju and Kidarite Steppe are side by side, Hephthalite Bactria/Tokharistan no longer covers the Turkic steppe, Samanid Khorasan sits beside Ghaznavid Ghazna, and Khwarazmian Khorasan sits beside the Ghurid core plus a short Ghur takeover fragment.
- v125 Middle East transition semantics split Sasanian/Byzantine provinces, Rashidun conquest fronts, Abbasid Baghdad/Persia/Egypt-Levant, Tahirid Khorasan, Fatimid Egypt/Levant, Ayyubid/Crusader/Mamluk Levant, Mongol/Ilkhanate Persia-Iraq, Seljuk Rum/Ottoman beylik, Ottoman-Safavid Iraq, and Palestine/Transjordan/Saudi mandate-era lanes; post-classical Middle East overlap is now removed from the sampled pass.
- v126 ancient Middle East semantics split Akkadian core/eastern pressure from Elam, Old Babylonian core from a short Elam campaign, Late Bronze / Iron Age southern Levant from Syro-Hittite northern Syria, Assyrian core from Babylonia's vassal/revolt phases, Neo-Elam from Persis/Susiana, and Achaemenid Persia from dated Anatolia, Babylonia, Levant, and Egyptian conquest fragments; sampled Middle East slot overlap is now zero.
- v127 Europe semantics split Roman Republic/Empire Italy-Greece-Gaul-Hispania-Britain phases, Western Roman withdrawal from Britain, World War II France/Poland/Italy occupation and resistance lanes, Nazi Germany core, neutral Spain continuity, and USSR core vs Warsaw Pact Poland influence; sampled Europe overlap is now zero.
- v128 East Asia semantics split Western Jin before/after the 280 conquest of Wu, Sui before/after the 589 conquest of Chen, Northern Song core vs southern consolidation after the Ten Kingdoms transition, and Unified/Late Silla vs early/unified Goryeo.
- v129 East Asia semantics split Qing Beijing/core and southern campaigns from Taiwan and Mongolia lanes; added a Taiwan island lane from Indigenous/Dutch/Zheng/Qing/Japanese/ROC phases; split Mongolia from Inner Mongol submission through Khalkha/Qing/Bogd/MPR phases; and split ROC-era China into early republic, warlord, Nanjing, wartime occupation, civil-war, PRC mainland, and ROC Taiwan fragments.
- v130 East Asia semantics added a Manchuria/Northeast lane from Later Jin and Qing Manchuria through Fengtian/Northeast Army, Japanese occupation, Manchukuo, Soviet occupation, and Communist Northeast base areas; split Korea's 1945-48 liberation/occupation transition before ROK/DPRK; and replaced the old Taisho/Showa rectangle with Taisho Japan, imperial Showa Japan, Allied occupation, and postwar Showa constitutional Japan.
- v131 South Asia semantics split Aurangzeb's Mughal maximum into North Indian core, Deccan, Bengal, and northwest frontier fragments; split the British Raj into direct provincial lanes and princely-state paramountcy; and added explicit partition, Bangladesh, and Ceylon independence transition edges.
- v132 Middle East semantics split Ottoman west into Anatolian core, Ottoman Egypt / French occupation / Muhammad Ali / khedivate transition, Ottoman/Egyptian/Ottoman Levant phases, Ottoman Hejaz suzerainty, Arabian interior / Saudi states / Rashidi / Saudi unification / Hashemite Hejaz, and narrowed Palestine/Transjordan mandate half-lanes.
- v133 Middle East semantics split the broad Umayyad west block into Damascus/Levant core, Egypt, Arabia, Iraq, and Persia/Khorasan fragments; retargeted 711 Iberia conquest through the Umayyad North Africa lane; and documented Al-Andalus as dependent on Damascus before 756.
- v134 Central Asia semantics split Soviet Central Asia into 1920-24 Bukharan, Khorezm, Kazakh ASSR, and Turkestan transition fragments, then Uzbek/Turkmen/Kazakh/Tajik/Kyrgyz Soviet republic lanes and separate 1991 independence lanes.
- v135 visual semantics replaced clipped trapezoid/hourglass polity silhouettes with non-clipping orthogonal guide lines, so partial-control cues no longer create blank spaces that read as ownerless land.
- v136 interim visual semantics superseded v135 with true orthogonal/Tetris-like clipped polygons, but its permissive blank-cutout interpretation is no longer the active rule.
- v137 visual semantics supersedes the v136 blank-space interpretation: clipped orthogonal notches are valid only when the renderer finds an adjacent overlapping polity/force to fill the missing piece, so loss and gain interlock instead of exposing blank land.
- v138 extends v137 with explicit non-contiguous notch owners, allowing a missing polygon piece to be filled by a remote/extra fragment such as Taiwan, Manchuria, or the Arabian interior when adjacency is lost by chart abstraction. Ambiguous notches remain suppressed rather than guessed.
- v139 East Asia semantics replaces the over-broad `eastAsia.prc` rectangle with same-color but separately labeled PRC China-proper, Northeast, Tibet, and Xinjiang fragments; adds a western frontier lane for Tibet/Xinjiang predecessor phases; and shifts Mongolia/Korea/Japan/Vietnam/Taiwan right by one slot.
- v140 Central Asia semantics enriches ancient and medieval wide blocks with owner-conserving orthogonal polygons and explicit multi-owner notch sequences: BMAC / early Sogdiana / Achaemenid / Greco-Bactrian / Kushan / Kidarite / Abbasid / Qara-Khanid / Seljuk / Mongol / Chagatai / Golden Horde / Timurid fragments now distinguish oasis cores, steppe neighbors, Khorasan, Bactria, Gandhara, and non-contiguous southern projections.
- v141 layout invariant: `slotEnd` is the exclusive right boundary / occupied slot count for a region, not the final slot index. Every entity must satisfy `slot + width <= slotEnd`; region headers and offsets rely on this.
- v142 Southeast Asia semantics uses the user's accepted "same polity can have several non-contiguous blocks" rule: Funan is split into a lower-Mekong core plus a Malay/Gulf maritime-network fragment, both using owner-conserving orthogonal notches filled by Thai local cultures, Indonesian cultures, and Tarumanagara rather than blank cutouts.
- v142 also enriches early Southeast Asian metadata for Funan, Tarumanagara, Pyu, Chenla, Dvaravati, Champa continuity, and Barangay communities so the region reads as a structured historical system rather than a thin label row.
- v143 Africa semantics enriches the Nile / Horn / Carthage lanes without inventing new geometry: Kerma -> Egyptian Nubia -> Kush -> Meroe -> Christian Nubia, D'mt -> Pre-Axumite -> Axum -> Zagwe -> Solomonic Ethiopia, and Carthage -> Roman Africa now read as explicit owner-to-owner transitions.
- v143 treats the Bantu expansion as a historical process lane rather than a centralized state, preserving the "no ownerless blank" visual rule without making a false polity claim.
- v144 early Europe semantics enriches pre-Roman Europe without forcing every culture into a state model: Aegean -> Minoan -> Mycenaean -> Greek Dark Age -> polis -> Macedon is now a readable Greek-lane sequence, while Italic/Etruscan, Gallic/Celtic, Iberian/Celtiberian, and British/Celtic lanes have explicit owners before Roman takeover.
- v144 keeps prehistoric and cultural horizons labeled as cultural owners, not kingdoms, so the chart avoids blank land without making false statehood claims.
- v145 visual semantics adds per-entity, time-bounded orthogonal notches: a block can now cut only the exact segment that has an adjacent or explicitly linked owner, preventing valid Tetris-like shapes from being suppressed just because a fixed generic notch would have created blank land.
- v145 early Americas semantics fills the simplified Maya/Central America lane before and after Olmec influence with explicit Early Central America, Early Maya/Formative, and Zapotec/Isthmian cultural owners; Olmec influence, Maya Preclassic, Preclassic Mesoamerica, and Zapotec/Isthmian blocks now interlock through owner-filled polygon notches instead of reverting to rectangles.
- v145 also enriches early Americas metadata and connections for Archaic Mesoamerica, Caribbean island cultures, early Andes, precolonial Brazil, North American and Canadian Indigenous cultural lanes, Chavin, Early Intermediate, Mound Builders, Wari-Tiwanaku Middle Horizon, and Late Intermediate Andes.
- v146 South Asia semantics removes three previously suppressed polygon cases: Harappan Fringe now interlocks with Ganges-Yamuna and southern cultural owners, Sangam Kingdoms interlock with Mauryan / early Deccan / Satavahana neighbors, and Pandya's lower notch is filled by Delhi Deccan pressure.
- v146 adds early South Asia cultural-owner and regional-polity detail for Ganges-Yamuna cultures, Southern Cultures, Early Bengal, Lankan Prehistory, Deccan post-Maurya states, Anuradhapura, Pallava, Shahi, Pala, Delhi Northwest, and related transition edges.
- v147 Middle East semantics removes all six remaining Middle East suppressed polygon cases: Old Babylonian Elam pressure now interlocks with Old Babylon, Achaemenid and Parthian Mesopotamia cut toward their Persian/Iranian cores, Umayyad Arabia cuts toward Damascus, Crusader States interlock with a new Muslim Syria / Zangid-field half-lane, and Saudi Arabia occupies the Arabia lane with Transjordan filling its northern/western edge.
- v148 East Asia semantics removes all four remaining East Asia suppressed polygon cases: Western Jin Unified and Sui Unified stay full after their completed 280 / 589 conquests because no contemporaneous southern owner remains, while Later Jin interlocks with Ming and Qing China Proper interlocks with Qing Manchuria through explicit notch owners.
- v149 Europe semantics removes all five remaining Europe suppressed polygon cases by flipping old outside-facing notches toward meaningful owners: Roman Greece / Balkans now interlock with Roman Italian/core lanes, Napoleonic Italy interlocks with the French imperial core as a dependent satellite, and the Confederation of the Rhine interlocks with the French imperial core as protector power.
- v150 Central Asia / Africa / Southeast Asia semantics removes the final seven suppressed polygon cases: Kangju, Hephthalite, Göktürk, Samanid Khorasan, Swahili Coast, and Kediri now use precise time-bounded owner-filled notches, while Bukharan PSR stays full because its left edge is the chart boundary rather than a missing neighbor.
- v151 mobile layout removes the half-screen initial gap caused by mobile `--timeline-edge-pad`, keeping desktop edge-focus behavior while making the Chinese mobile first viewport start directly on the timeline.
- v152 early East Asia semantics applies the same no-ownerless-gap rule to first-screen cultural lanes: China Neolithic / Southern Cultures, Steppe Bronze / Early Nomads / Gojoseon, late Jomon / Yayoi, and Chinese-rule Vietnam now use owner-filled orthogonal cutouts only where a neighboring or explicitly linked remote owner carries the missing piece.
- v152 also records early East Asian cultural owners as cultural or legendary-archaeological abstractions in their detail text, so visible ownership does not imply modern borders or fully centralized statehood.
- v153 early Southeast Asia semantics enriches long Indonesian / Malay / Mekong / Thai basin / Myanmar / Philippine pre-state lanes as cultural owners, not empty placeholders and not modern nation-states projected backward.
- v153 deliberately avoids adding new polygons where the timeline already has clean same-lane succession; the stronger correction is metadata plus relationship edges showing how Funan, Tarumanagara, Pyu, Dvaravati, Srivijaya, and Barangay polities emerge from inhabited cultural networks.
- v154 Europe migration-era semantics enriches Germanic, Lusatian, West Slavic, early steppe, Scythian, East Slavic, Anglo-Saxon, Piast, and Kyivan Rus lanes as cultural or state-forming owners rather than thin labels or blank predecessors.
- v154 post-Roman Italy semantics splits the old broad Byzantine Italy block into a short Justinianic reconquest, side-by-side Byzantine Exarchate / Lombard Italy half-lanes, a late Lombard phase, and Frankish Italy before the 800 Carolingian imperial block. This removes the old 774-800 Italy owner gap and avoids pretending Byzantium owned all Italy from 568 to 751.
- v155 early Middle East semantics enriches Anatolian, Hattian, early Egyptian, Canaanite, and early Arabian long lanes as cultural or state-building owners rather than thin labels or blank pre-state placeholders.
- v155 Arabian lane semantics splits old full-width `arabia_roman` into half-width `Arabia Petraea` plus a same-period `Independent Arabia` half-lane, so Roman annexation of Nabataea no longer implies ownership of all Arabia and the non-Roman half remains visibly owned.
- v156 ancient Middle East semantics enriches Sumer, Gutian, Ur III, Isin-Larsa, Kassite Babylonia, Post-Kassite Babylonia, Middle/Neo-Elam, Neo-Hittite Anatolia, and Third Intermediate Egypt as explicit owner chains rather than silent broad placeholders.
- v156 deliberately keeps clean same-lane chronological succession as full-width continuity with strong metadata and relationship links; orthogonal notches remain reserved for simultaneous partial control, neighboring owner fills, remote occupation, or influence fragments that another entity can visibly carry.
- v157 Europe semantics applies the same rule to medieval and early-modern long lanes: Frankish -> Carolingian -> West/East Francia -> Capetian / HRE, Valois -> Bourbon -> Revolutionary France, Golden Horde/Rus -> Muscovy -> Russia, Ottoman Balkans -> Greece, and Poland-Lithuania -> partition zones are now explicit owner chains.
- v157 splits old `poland_partition` into Prussian/German, Austrian, and Russian owner fragments, using non-contiguous simplified-grid ownership rather than a single ambiguous full-width block or blank land after the Commonwealth disappears.
- v158 early China semantics adds owner-filled orthogonal southern-edge interlocks for Xia, Shang, Western Zhou, and Eastern Zhou. The interlocks are filled by Southern Cultures, Chu, and the short Qin Southern Conquest fragment rather than blank cutouts.
- v158 keeps completed same-lane conquest phases full-width after the conquest is complete: Qin begins as a full two-slot imperial block only in 221 BCE, while the 223-221 BCE Chu-to-Qin transfer is a separate southern fragment so no land is ownerless between Chu and Qin.
- v159 early South Asia semantics accepts non-contiguous / cultural owner fragments where the simplified grid hides real neighbors: Late Harappan Northwest and Late Harappan Fringe now bridge Mature Harappan decline to Vedic lanes, while the fringe's orthogonal cutouts are explicitly filled by Ganges-Yamuna and southern cultural owners.
- v159 keeps sparse early evidence honest: Vedic lanes are visible cultural/polity horizons, while Gandhara and Bengal States are visible owners with notes explaining their frontier/delta evidence limits rather than treating them as blank space. v160 moves the Vedic lanes and related archaeological/cultural owners into the first-class `culture` category instead of leaving them under a league/confederation label.
- v160 category semantics makes `culture` a first-class filter, legend item, URL category, and block accent. Cultural horizons, archaeological cultures, and migration/process owner lanes should use `category: 'culture'` when the chart needs an owner without implying centralized statehood.
- v160 also broadens the old `confederation` category's visible label to League/联盟 and keeps `Confederation`, `Federation`, `联邦`, and `邦联` as URL aliases, so old shared links remain valid without making every multi-polity lane sound like a modern federal state.
- v161 early Africa semantics applies the culture-owner rule to the chart's weakest long early lanes: Horn, Nubian, Maghreb, Sahel, Guinea Coast, Southern African, Nok, and Post-Nok cultural owners now make early African lanes inhabited and connected without inventing centralized states or modern borders.
- v161 keeps clean same-lane succession full-width where no simultaneous visible neighbor carries a missing piece. In those cases, the correct no-ownerless-gap move is stronger metadata plus relationship links; orthogonal polygons remain reserved for actual simultaneous partial control, frontier influence, occupation, or explicit adjacent/remote owner fills.
- v162 Sri Lanka/Ceylon semantics applies split-owner logic to a historically important island lane: Portuguese, Dutch, and early British coastal phases now interlock with the Kandyan interior, and full-width British Ceylon begins only after the 1815 Kandyan Convention.
- v162 confirms the user's newer rule as an ongoing design principle: when the simplified grid hides real-world neighbors, use adjacent or non-contiguous owner fragments when they are historically meaningful; only use full-width continuity when the transfer is complete or when a cultural/process owner is the more honest abstraction.
- v163 early Central Asia semantics applies the culture-owner rule to the chart's highest-scoring placeholder blocks: Steppe, Mountain, and Afghan cultural lanes now have categories, centers, territory notes, detail text, wiki mappings, and relationship links into BMAC, early Sogdiana, Saka/Scythian steppe ownership, and Achaemenid satrapal fragments.
- v163 deliberately keeps the early Central Asian Steppe / Mountain / Afghan cultural lanes full-width because they are parallel simplified owner strips rather than a documented partial-control transfer; the no-ownerless-gap correction is explicit cultural ownership and successor links, not decorative notches.
- v164 late Southeast Asia semantics applies the owner-conserving rule to Post-Srivijaya, Late Khmer, Post-Angkor Cambodia, Fragmented Burma, Malacca, Java's Islamic sultanates, Spanish Philippines, and Pagan. The concrete territorial-pressure cases use orthogonal filled notches; plural internal mosaics stay full-width but are categorized and described as multi-owner fields.
- v164 adds three new owner-filled Southeast Asian interlocks: Post-Srivijaya's late Java-facing edge is filled by Majapahit, Late Khmer's Siam-facing edge by Sukhothai / early Ayutthaya, and Post-Angkor Cambodia's Siam-facing edge by Ayutthaya, Toungoo Siam, restored Ayutthaya, Thonburi, and Rattanakosin.
- v165 Mesoamerica semantics applies the same rule to the highest-scoring Americas placeholders: Epiclassic and Postclassic central Mexican blocks are now plural city-state fields, with the formerly blank southern strip carried by Xochicalco / Cholula / Mixtec-Puebla / Zapotec corridor fragments.
- v165 uses a cascading owner-fill chain rather than fake precision: central Mexico notches into the southern corridor fragments, and those fragments notch into Classic/Postclassic Maya continuities. This expresses remote/split owners where the simplified grid lacks all real neighbors, while preserving Maya polities as separate owners.
- v167 Sudan semantics applies the same owner-conserving rule to the Nile / western Sudan lane: early Funj/Sennar succeeds Christian Nubia, later Sennar narrows beside Darfur, Turco-Egyptian Nile Sudan occupies the eastern corridor before Darfur's incorporation, then Egyptian Sudan, Mahdist State, Anglo-Egyptian Sudan, and independent Sudan continue the chain.
- v167 also codifies a rendering rule for extremely short phases: if a block is too short to contain text cleanly, the block face suppresses its internal label while keeping the full accessible label, tooltip, search identity, and detail panel. Dense accuracy should not create illegible labels.
- v168 Central Asia semantics corrects the khanate-era owner chain: Kokand no longer begins in 1507, `fergana_begliks` carries the pre-Kokand valley/mountain owner field, and Bukhara / Khiva / Kazakh / Fergana-Kokand / Afghan-route / Russian conquest phases interlock through owner-filled orthogonal notches.
- v168 accepts non-contiguous or edge-owner abstractions where the simplified grid hides real neighbors, but every cutout still needs a named owner and a territory note explaining whether the owner is a state, protectorate, local field, cultural process, or frontier corridor.
- v185 modern Middle East semantics confirms that some misleading rectangles need chronological splitting rather than notches: Egypt must separate protectorate, kingdom, and republic phases; Iraq must separate mandate, kingdom, and republic phases; and the mandate-era Levant needs parallel Palestine / French Syria-Lebanon / Transjordan strips plus short independence bridges before the post-1948 composite lane.
- v185 verification confirms the current design rule: use non-contiguous owner fragments and filled orthogonal cuts when they clarify a concrete territorial recipient, but prefer chronological splitting when the visual problem is a misleading phase label rather than an actual spatial contraction.
- v186 Afghan-route semantics shows the same rule in a gap case: a long label like `Islamic Afghanistan` can be worse than a missing polygon when it implies a full owner replacement that sources do not support. The fix is a continuous named-owner chain across Turk Shahi, Kabul/Zabul, Saffarid, and Ghaznavid phases, not a generic blank or one over-broad Islamic rectangle.
- Remaining shape-suppression work is now at 0 known cases; the next territory-semantics pass should audit broad rectangles, placeholder metadata, and high-impact date transitions under the same rule: use explicit adjacent or non-contiguous owner fragments instead of leaving notches or expansion gaps visually ownerless.
- v249-v254 response to the latest review: keep same-color blocks as separate records while hiding only their internal seam borders, keep Ming Zheng / Tungning in Taiwan raw `slot 8` and current render layout slot 5, continue filling high-value blank-looking bands through source-backed owner chains, and make dark-mode fills lower-saturation / darker with light labels.
- v249 filled the Middle East Egypt-Levant AD 868-969 Tulunid / Abbasid Egypt / Ikhshidid sequence; v250-v251 filled the Central Asia Afghanistan chain from Mughal Afghanistan through Hotak, Afsharid, Durrani, Barakzai, and independent Afghanistan, including Kokand edge owner fills.
- Current residual work is qualitative rather than a claim of perfection: keep auditing dense connection-label readability, the large right-side relationship rail, other metadata debt, Korean Empire / Russia / modern Americas candidates, and additional world-history refinement.

## v169 Post-Songhai Sahel Audit Notes
- The post-v168 weak-row audit identified `sahel_fragmented` (1591-1800) as the highest-scoring weak entity: a full gray block with no category, description, detail metadata, representative center, territory note, or relationship links.
- The same lane also had overbroad follow-on blocks: full-width Sokoto, French West Africa, and modern Sahel implied one owner across western/central Sahel plus northern Nigeria even though the simplified map can represent a west/east split.
- Design direction: keep the lane owner-conserving but not overfit every real-world neighbor. Use two simplified sub-lanes: a western/central Niger Bend chain and an eastern Dendi/Hausaland/Northern Nigeria chain. Where a block narrows, the adjacent block explicitly fills the notch.

## v169 Source Notes
- Britannica's Songhai page supports the 1591 Moroccan firearm conquest after Tondibi and the Moroccan control of Timbuktu/Gao economic centers (`https://www.britannica.com/place/Songhai-empire`).
- EBSCO's Arma/Timbuktu research starter supports the Moroccan expedition, Arma military caste, Timbuktu-centered pashalik, and later autonomous local pashas (`https://www.ebsco.com/research-starters/history/rise-arma-timbuktu`).
- Britannica's western Africa survey supports the Songhai kings being pushed into Dendi, Mande power shifting to Bambara Segu/Kaarta, and Arma descendants becoming tributary to desert pastoralists by the 18th century (`https://www.britannica.com/place/western-Africa/The-Islamic-revolution-in-the-western-Sudan`).
- Britannica's Bambara states page supports Segu/Kaarta, Mamari Kulibali around 1712, Segu expansion, and Bambara collapse before Macina pressure (`https://www.britannica.com/place/Bambara-states`).
- Britannica's Tukulor empire page supports Umar Tall conquering Segu in 1861, Macina afterward, and French conquest after 1890 (`https://www.britannica.com/place/Tukulor-empire`).
- Britannica's Usman dan Fodio / Nigeria pages support the 1804 jihad, Sokoto/Gwandu capitals, British subjugation of Fulani emirs, and Sokoto falling in 1903 (`https://www.britannica.com/place/western-Africa/The-jihad-of-Usman-dan-Fodio`, `https://www.britannica.com/place/Nigeria/The-arrival-of-the-British`).
- Britannica's French West Africa and Nigeria colonial pages support the 1895-1958 French West Africa frame, 1960 independence of former French territories, Northern Nigeria's colonial frame, and Nigeria's 1960 independence (`https://www.britannica.com/place/French-West-Africa`, `https://www.britannica.com/place/Nigeria/Nigeria-as-a-colony`).

## v170 Post-Maurya Northwest Audit Notes
- The post-v169 weak-row audit ranked `indo_greek` as the highest-scoring remaining weak entity: it had no category, description, detail metadata, representative center, territory note, or relationship links.
- The same post-Maurya South Asia cluster also had weak Shunga, Kanva, Indo-Scythian, and Indo-Parthian rows. The main semantic risk was that Indo-Scythian/Saka pressure sat in the compressed northern lane without explaining that it represents western/northwestern owners rather than a modern all-India state.
- Design direction: keep the existing South Asia lanes, but add explicit metadata and two precise non-contiguous owner-filled bites. Indo-Greek's late loss and Indo-Parthian's early edge are filled by the Indo-Scythian/Saka owner instead of turning into unexplained cutouts.

## v174 East Asia Vietnam Owner-Semantics Audit Notes
- After v173, the metadata-thickness audit ranked East Asia highest again. The most visible weakness was not Chinese-rule Vietnam anymore, but the post-939 Vietnam lane: a broad Later Le rectangle and a long Nguyen block hid Mac, restored Le, Trinh, Nguyen Lords, Tay Son, and French colonial ownership.
- Design decision: use side-by-side half-lanes before cutting decorative notches. The simplified grid cannot show every real-world neighbor, but it can show the main north/south political owners. For this pass, owner-filled adjacency is more honest than fake trapezoids or unclaimed gaps.
- Accepted tradeoff: Modern Vietnam remains one post-1945 block for now. Splitting DRV / Republic of Vietnam / reunification is a later Cold War-specific pass, because this round focused on the precolonial-to-colonial owner chain.

## v175 South Asia Early-Medieval Owner-Semantics Audit Notes
- User feedback emphasized that shrinkage should usually mean another named owner gains space; blank notches are only acceptable when the abstraction cannot responsibly identify an owner. The improved design therefore permits adjacent half-lanes, non-contiguous frontier owners, and composite owner labels.
- The post-v174 weakness audit ranked South Asia highest. The clearest visual problem was the southern lane: `pallava` and `chola` were long, full-width rectangles that erased Chalukya, Rashtrakuta, Western Chalukya, and other Deccan owners.
- Design decision: split the southern lane into Deccan and Tamil halves instead of adding decorative trapezoids. This keeps horizontal/vertical sides and makes territorial change read as interlocking owner pieces.
- Accepted tradeoff: `deccan_successors` is a composite abstraction for Yadava, Hoysala, Kakatiya, and related plateau powers. It is more honest than blank space, but it should eventually be split if the South Asia row receives a higher-resolution medieval pass.

## v175 Source Notes
- Encyclopaedia Iranica supports Kidarite rule in Tokharistan and later Gandhara, with loss of Tokharistan to the Hephthalites in 467 and residual North Indian/Gandhara presence (`https://www.iranicaonline.org/articles/kidarites/`).
- Britannica supports Harsha as ruler of a large northern Indian empire from 606 to 647 and as a transition point from ancient to medieval regional competition (`https://www.britannica.com/biography/Harsha`).
- Britannica supports Rashtrakuta Deccan dominance, replacement of Chalukya power, the Kanchi reach, Ellora/Kailasa, and the Chalukya/Western Chalukya date frame used for the half-lanes (`https://www.britannica.com/topic/Rashtrakuta-dynasty`, `https://www.britannica.com/biography/Pulakeshin-II`).
- Britannica supports Pala rule in Bihar and Bengal from the 8th to 12th century, Gopala's rise, Dharmapala's expansion, and the Kannauj contest (`https://www.britannica.com/topic/Pala-dynasty`).
- Britannica supports Ghaznavid rule in Khorasan, Afghanistan, and northern India, Ghurid expansion under Ghiyath/Muizz al-Din, and Delhi Sultanate formation through Ghurid campaigns and Qutb ud-Din Aibak (`https://www.britannica.com/topic/Ghaznavid-dynasty`, `https://www.britannica.com/place/Ghurid-sultanate`, `https://www.britannica.com/place/Delhi-sultanate`).

## v176 Cutout-Owner Interaction Audit Notes
- The data model now prevents ownerless clipped notches, but the user still has to infer too much from tiny geometry on the canvas.
- The highest-leverage usability issue is therefore interpretability: every filled cutout should explain who owns that piece, whose contraction it represents, and whether the owner is adjacent or remote/composite.
- Design decision: make `territory-fill-piece` elements real interactive map objects rather than passive decoration. The action opens the owner detail panel because the user is most likely asking, "Who took this piece?"

## v176 Cutout-Owner Interaction Pass

- Added tooltip copy showing owner name, represented years, adjacent vs remote/composite status, and the source entity whose cutout is being filled.
- Added map highlights for both the source block and the owner block while a fill piece is active.
- Changed detail-panel `Cutout Owners` / `缺口承接` rows into jump links that navigate to the owner entity.
- Updated README and active assets to `v176`.

## v187 Japan Muromachi / Sengoku Owner-Fill Plan
- User feedback clarified that the intended grammar is Tetris-like ownership conservation: if one country loses a piece, another adjacent, remote, or composite owner should visibly receive it; blank cutouts should be avoided unless truly unavoidable.
- Selected the Japan medieval-to-early-modern chain because audit data showed `muromachi`, `kamakura`, `heian`, and `azuchi` were high-visibility weak blocks with too little detail/relationship context.
- Design choice: same-lane successions such as Heian -> Kamakura -> Edo should remain full blocks with richer details and relationship links, while late Muromachi specifically gets an owner-filled polygon because the Onin War / Sengoku transition is a concrete fragmentation of effective control.
- Implemented `sengoku_daimyo` as a composite, non-contiguous owner from 1467 to 1573 and filled `muromachi`'s late right-edge orthogonal cutout with it.
- Added source-backed descriptions, details, capitals/centers, territory notes, wiki mappings, event markers, and relationship links for Heian, Kamakura, Muromachi, Sengoku Daimyo, Azuchi-Momoyama, Edo, and Meiji.

## v189 Late Southeast Asia Owner-Fill Plan
- User feedback clarified the visual target again: blocks should feel like orthogonal, Tetris-like polygons where territorial contraction is paired with another named owner; trapezoids, plain rectangles, and ownerless holes are too ambiguous.
- Accepted non-contiguous owner fragments as a necessary abstraction when the simplified grid cannot place every real-world neighbor adjacent to the contracting entity. The rule remains conservative: use explicit remote/composite owners only when the receiving owner is historically legible.
- Selected late Southeast Asia because the current chain had high-value weak points around Malacca/Malaya/Malaysia, Restored Toungoo/Konbaung/British Burma/Myanmar, Rattanakosin/Siam-Thailand, French Indochina, and the Spanish/American/independent Philippines succession.
- Design decisions:
  - Use relationship links and richer metadata for same-lane successions such as Portuguese Malacca -> Dutch Malacca -> British Malaya -> Malaysia and Spanish Philippines -> American Philippines -> Philippines.
  - Use orthogonal owner-filled cutouts only where another owner receives a visible lost strip: Rattanakosin/Siam-Thailand's late eastern edge is filled by French Indochina and post-1954 Indochina states; Konbaung's late right edge is filled by a non-contiguous British Lower Burma strip.
  - Keep British Lower Burma as a clean narrow recipient strip rather than giving it a counter-notch, so the visual grammar remains readable instead of recursively nested.
  - Fix hidden modal backdrop pointer events so owner-fill strips remain clickable after opening and closing detail panels.

## v191 Italy Risorgimento-to-Republic Owner-Fill Plan
- Current audit ranked Europe as the largest remaining metadata-debt region, and `italy_states` / `italy_republic` were among the weakest individual rows. Italy is also a high-fit response to the user's latest direction because 1815 restoration, 1861 incomplete unification, and 1943 wartime division all have concrete named owners for lost or unincorporated space.
- Design decision: do not create decorative polygons where there is no receiving owner. The old `fascist_italy` hourglass marker has been removed; territorial geometry now appears only where a named owner fills the cutout.
- Added three new owner fragments:
  - `sardinia_piedmont` fills the left / unification-engine share of post-Vienna Italy.
  - `austrian_italy` fills the right / northeastern Austrian hegemony share of post-Vienna Italy.
  - `italy_unincorporated` fills the early Kingdom of Italy's missing Venetia + papal Rome share until the 1866-70 completion of unification.
- Added reciprocal owner-filled cutouts for the 1943 split: `italy_cobelligerent` is filled by `nazi_italy_occupation`, and `nazi_italy_occupation` is filled by `italy_cobelligerent`.
- Enriched 9 Italy target entities with descriptions, detail metadata, centers/capitals, territory notes, categories/rulers, wiki mappings, relationship links, and Europe event markers.

## v191 Italy Source Notes
- Britannica supports the 1815 Vienna restoration, Austrian Lombardy-Venetia, restored Papal/Two Sicilies/Tuscan/ducal states, Austrian hegemony, and Sardinia-Piedmont standing outside the Austrian system (`https://www.britannica.com/place/Italy/The-restoration-period`).
- Britannica's Risorgimento page supports the 1815-1870 frame, the 1861 Kingdom of Italy, Piedmont's leadership, and the later annexation of Venetia in 1866 and papal Rome in 1870 (`https://www.britannica.com/event/Risorgimento`).
- The U.S. Office of the Historian supports Piedmont-Sardinia being reconstituted and enlarged with Genoa after Vienna, Victor Emmanuel II becoming king of Italy in 1861, and the capital sequence Turin -> Florence -> Rome (`https://history.state.gov/countries/piedmont-sardinia`).
- Britannica supports the October 1922 March on Rome / Mussolini appointment (`https://www.britannica.com/event/March-on-Rome`).
- The National WWII Museum supports the September 1943 armistice, co-belligerent status, German occupation, Badoglio/king flight to Brindisi, and Mussolini's September 23 Italian Social Republic / Salo Republic (`https://www.nationalww2museum.org/war/articles/allied-campaign-italy-1943-45-timeline-part-one`).
- Britannica supports the 1946 referendum in favor of the republic and the postwar constituent assembly (`https://www.britannica.com/place/Italy/Italy-since-1945`).

## v192 Label-Fitting Visual Polish Plan
- Evidence from the v191 mobile check left three old Europe narrow labels overflowing in Chinese: `roman_transalpine_gaul`, `byzantine_exarchate`, and `lombard_italy`.
- First fix: add compact face labels for those three while preserving full names in detail/search/accessibility:
  - `roman_transalpine_gaul`: `Nar` / `纳尔`
  - `byzantine_exarchate`: `Rav` / `拉文`
  - `lombard_italy`: `Lom` / `伦巴`
- Browser follow-up exposed a broader desktop-English problem: many narrow legacy blocks could still render clipped face text. Design decision: add render-time label fitting instead of hand-maintaining dozens of one-off short labels. If a block's visible face label does not fit its measured width after render, the face label is hidden while the full name remains available via click, keyboard focus, search, tooltip, and detail panel.
- Active assets now load `styles.css?v=192`, `print.css?v=192`, and `app.js?v=192`.

## v193 Adaptive Label-Fitting Plan
- v192 solved visible overflow but reduced information density because many narrow blocks became blank on the face.
- v193 changes the fitting ladder from "full label -> hide" to "full label -> compact generated label -> hide":
  - English generated labels use significant-word initials first (`Polish People's Republic` -> `PPR`, `Soviet Bloc Poland` -> `SBP`) and then shorter prefixes if needed.
  - Chinese generated labels use the first two characters, then a one-character fallback.
  - Existing curated `shortName` / `shortNameCN` values remain the first visible choice.
- This keeps the no-overflow invariant while recovering scan hints for most formerly hidden blocks.
- Active assets now load `styles.css?v=193`, `print.css?v=193`, and `app.js?v=193`.

## v194 Korea Occupation-Zone Owner-Fill Plan
- User feedback refined the standard again: the chart should not settle for rectangles, trapezoids, or visually blank holes when it is trying to show territorial change. If land/control leaves one entity, another historically reasonable owner or force should visibly carry the missing piece, including non-contiguous fragments where the simplified grid cannot place every real-world neighbor.
- Current audit found a concrete semantic failure in the East Asia lane: the old `korea_liberation_occupation` hourglass shape described U.S. and Soviet zones, but because it had no explicit owners the renderer could resolve cutouts through incidental neighboring lanes. That satisfied the "not blank" rule mechanically while failing the "reasonable owner" rule.
- Design decision: replace the single gray Korea liberation/occupation block with two explicit 1945-48 fragments, `korea_us_occupation` and `korea_soviet_occupation`, each with reciprocal full-period orthogonal cutouts. The owners are named authorities at the 38th parallel, not a generic blank or accidental adjacency.
- Follow-up audit caught another automatic-adjacent problem created by the split: post-1945 Japan-proper phases with decorative left cutouts could read the Korean lane as a recipient. v194 removes those decorative cutouts from `showa_imperial_japan`, `allied_occupation_japan`, and `postwar_showa_japan`; their notes now state that Korea/Taiwan/Manchuria/occupied China are separate lanes, not owner-filled missing pieces of Japan proper.
- Small label polish: add curated face labels for the last two v193 all-region hidden-label cases, `benin_early` and `ashanti`, while preserving full labels in detail/search/accessibility.
- Source grounding for the Korea split comes from the U.S. Office of the Historian, Britannica, and the U.S. National Archives on the 38th-parallel U.S./Soviet occupation zones and the 1948 separate-state transition.

## v195 Automatic Adjacent-Fill Audit Plan
- User feedback clarified the tradeoff: non-contiguous fragments are acceptable when they make missing land/control more precise, but the site still needs judgment because the simplified grid cannot represent every real-world neighbor.
- Audit target: all automatically resolved adjacent owner fills, especially cases where a shape was originally decorative rather than a documented transfer.
- Highest-risk current case: Soviet Central Asia in the early 1920s. `turkestan_transition` used an hourglass that could let Afghanistan appear as the owner of a Soviet Turkestan cutout; `khorezm_psr`, `kazakh_assr_early`, `tajik_assr`, and `kyrgyz_soviet_early` also had decorative shapes that implied nearby Soviet lanes were receiving pieces. The VM verifier then exposed the same pattern in East Asia: `jp_korea` could auto-fill from `mongolia_bogd`.
- Design decision: remove those decorative cutouts rather than invent false receiving owners. The 1924 national-territorial delimitation is already visible through the successor lanes and half-width Tajik/Kyrgyz split; Japanese Korea's colonial status is already visible as its own lane. Adding notches in these cases lowers accuracy.
- Source grounding: the 1929 VTsIK decree text hosted by Seventeen Moments in Soviet History documents the Soviet delimitation logic; Britannica's Central Asia overview grounds the broader Soviet creation of five Central Asian republics.

## v196 Mesoamerican Contact-vs-Ownership Plan

Letting those rows generate owner-fill cutouts turns cultural contact into land ownership.

## v200 Warsaw Pact Influence-vs-Ownership Plan

If the missing share has a concrete recipient, use a named adjacent or remote/composite owner fragment. ## v204 Mesoamerica Owner-Continuity Plan
- The next highest-risk adjacent-fill case was `aztec_southern_tribute` resolving its southern tribute-frontier taper into `maya_post`. That made Aztec tributary pressure look like a territorial transfer into the Maya lane, and the automatic fill could run beyond the old Maya Postclassic end date.
- Design decision: do not draw a notch when the real relationship is tribute hegemony or frontier pressure. Keep `Aztec Tribute Frontier` whole, then make the post-1521 Maya / Central America lane richer with named phases: `Maya Conquest Frontier` (1521-1543), a narrowed `New Spain: Central America` core (1543-1697) beside `Independent Maya Holdouts`, full colonial Central America after Nojpeten falls in 1697, and a 1821-1823 `Central America in Mexican Empire` bridge before the United Provinces.

Jones supports Nojpeten's 1697 fall as the last unconquered native New World kingdom; Britannica supports the 1821 independence / 1823 United Provinces sequence.

## v205 Champa / Đại Việt Orthogonal Owner Plan
- The next user-facing issue was the Champa / Đại Việt visualization: opposing tapers made two long-coexisting polities look like they were mutually owning each other's missing strips, and the old geometry did not show the post-1471 Cham residual polity.
- Design decision: use one Tetris-like orthogonal expanding-owner polygon for the compressed Vietnamese state lane. `Đại Việt / Vietnam` now spans 1009-1863 across the Vietnam slot with two explicit cutouts: `Champa` fills the 1009-1471 left half before Vijaya falls, and `Panduranga Cham Remnant` fills the 1471-1835 right quarter as a non-contiguous Cham residual owner.
- The chart therefore keeps the user's no-ownerless-land rule while avoiding false automatic adjacency. The conquest is visible as Vietnamese widening in 1471, but the Cham residual remains named and clickable until the 1832 annexation / 1833-35 resistance endpoint.
- Source grounding: Britannica supports Lê Thánh Tông's 1471 defeat of Champa and reduction of Champa to a southern remnant; Cambridge Core supports the 1470-1509 Champa crisis and the 1832-35 disappearance/integration of the last principality of Pāṇḍuraṅga; Kyoto Review supports the 1693-1835 Vietnam-Champa relationship and final resistance.

## v207 Visual Semantics + Manchuria Owner-Continuity Plan
- User feedback highlighted four immediate interpretability issues: same-color adjacent blocks looked like one owner but retained visible seams; Chinese narrow labels could render upside down; connection arrows needed a separate text-label toggle; and the Manchuria / Northeast lane looked ownerless before Later Jin.
- Design decision: treat same-color seam suppression as a visual merge, not a data merge. Only exact same base-color blocks in the same region whose rendered edges touch get internal seam classes; hover/focus restores the border so details remain separable.
- Design decision: keep the user's owner-conserving rule for blank spaces, but do not invent a literal neighbor when the compressed grid loses adjacency. For pre-1616 Manchuria, add a named owner chain and allow broad powers to have companion fragments in non-adjacent lanes.
- Implemented a separate `showConnectionLabels` / `linkLabels=0|1` layer: arrows stay visible when text labels are off.
- Implemented the first v207 data pass for Manchuria / Northeast: `Early Manchurian Peoples` -> `Fuyu / Buyeo` -> `Goguryeo North` -> `Tang-Mohe Transition` -> `Bohai / Parhae` -> `Liao Manchuria` -> `Jurchen Jin Manchuria` -> `Yuan Liaoyang` -> `Ming Liaodong / Jurchens` -> Later Jin and existing modern Northeast phases.
- Updated descriptions, details, centers/capitals, wiki mappings, relationship links, event markers, dark-mode palette, Chinese narrow-label CSS, active assets to `v207`, and documentation.
- Source grounding: Britannica supports historical Manchuria names and the Yuan Liaoyang / Ming Liaodong / Jurchen-Later Jin sequence; Britannica supports Parhae/Bohai in northern Manchuria and northern Korea; Britannica supports Jurchen Jin as a Manchurian Jurchen empire; Britannica's Korea article supports Buyeo in the Sungari basin of Manchuria.
- Verification passed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, active asset scan, and VM integrity for the new Manchuria IDs with no missing entities, details, capitals, or bad connection endpoints. The East Asia Manchuria slot now covers -3000 to 2000 continuously.

- Remaining open design issue: the column order still needs a principled adjacency-cost algorithm. East Asia's linear order cannot satisfy all 2D relationships, and Taiwan/China/Japan distance should be handled by a ranked slot-ordering pass rather than ad hoc swaps.

## v208 East Asia Slot-Group Layout Plan
- User feedback identified the strongest remaining cognitive-layout failure: Taiwan was farther from the China core than Japan was. The old implementation used raw historical `slot` directly for rendering, so data semantics and screen order were the same thing.
- Design decision: split slot semantics from render layout. Historical data keeps original `slot` / `width` values; rendering computes a `layoutSlot` through a cached region layout. Territory cutouts and adjacent-owner detection still use raw slots, so the layout pass cannot silently rewrite ownership semantics.
- Design decision: optimize lane groups, not individual slots. Any slots crossed by a wide entity are merged into one group first, so a two-slot block such as unified China remains visually contiguous after reordering.
- Implementation target: add a generic slot-group optimizer with connection-type weights and optional region guides. Activate it first only for East Asia to avoid unreviewed global reshuffles. Other regions keep original order until they are audited.
- East Asia guide: Tibet/Xinjiang -> Steppe/Mongolia -> Manchuria/Northeast -> Vietnam -> China core/south -> Taiwan -> Korea -> Japan. This makes China adjacent to Vietnam and Taiwan, keeps Korea/Japan paired, and makes Taiwan closer to China than Japan.
- Active assets now load `styles.css?v=208`, `print.css?v=208`, and `app.js?v=208`.
- Verification passed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, active asset scan with `v208`, VM layout audit, and VM data integrity with 8 regions, 794 entities, 698 connections, no duplicate IDs, no missing endpoints, no unknown categories, no invalid owners, no unresolved shapes, and complete layout coverage for every region.
- East Asia layout verification passed: rendered order is `[3] [4] [2] [7] [0+1] [8] [5] [6]`; raw Taiwan slot remains `8`, rendered Taiwan layout slot is `6`, Taiwan-China distance is 2 layout slots / 112px, Japan-China distance is 4 layout slots / 224px, and Korea-Japan distance is 1 layout slot / 56px.
- Browser verification passed on desktop Chinese East Asia and 390px Chinese mobile using only `v208` assets. Both rendered 151 blocks, 58 owner-fill pieces, 132 connection paths, no horizontal overflow, and no console/runtime errors; `linkLabels=0` still removes all SVG text labels while preserving paths.
- Temporary browser-validation server on `127.0.0.1:8765` was stopped after QA.

## v209 Three Kingdoms Owner-Split Plan
- User feedback asked for richer Three Kingdoms detail and for territory loss to be visibly received by another owner rather than becoming blank space. The old `shu_wu` composite solved the no-blank problem but collapsed Shu Han and Eastern Wu into one southern rectangle.
- Source grounding: Britannica's Three Kingdoms page supports the 220-280 frame, Shu-Han proclaimed in Sichuan in 221 and conquered by Wei in 263/264, Wu declared south of the Yangtze at Jianye in 222 and conquered by Jin in 280. Britannica's Sun Quan and Wu pages support Wu's lower-Yangtze/Jianye focus and 222-280 duration.
- Design decision: split formal states from short territorial-control bridges. `liu_bei_shu_domain` (220-221) and `sun_quan_wu_domain` (220-222) prevent tiny ownerless gaps without backdating formal dynasty dates. `shu_han` (221-263) and `eastern_wu` (222-280) then carry the two southern Three Kingdoms halves.
- Design decision: after Shu falls, the left half is not blank. `wei_shu_commanderies` (263-266) uses Cao Wei's color and `jin_shu_commanderies` (266-280) uses Western Jin's color, so same-color adjacency makes Wei/Jin visibly widen while Eastern Wu remains separate until 280.
- Replaced all application references to `shu_wu` with the six new entities, added descriptions, detail metadata, capitals, wiki mappings, relationship links, and East Asia events for `Wei Conquers Shu Han` (263) and `Jin Conquers Eastern Wu` (280).
- Updated the `chinese_vn` remote-owner chain: after Eastern Han it now passes through `sun_quan_wu_domain` and `eastern_wu`, then unified Jin, Eastern Jin, Southern Dynasties, unified Sui, Tang, and Ten Kingdoms.
- Active assets now load `styles.css?v=209`, `print.css?v=209`, and `app.js?v=209`.

- VM target checks confirmed the old `shu_wu` ID is absent from app sources, all six v209 IDs have descriptions/details/capitals, and `chinese_vn` fills through `sun_quan_wu_domain` and `eastern_wu`.

Desktop with labels on rendered 276 SVG connection text nodes; mobile with `linkLabels=0` rendered 0 SVG text nodes while preserving all paths.

## v210 Sixteen Kingdoms / Former Qin Owner-Split Plan
- User feedback accepted non-contiguous and composite fragments where the simplified grid lacks every real-world neighbor, but still asked that gaps be filled by reasonable owners rather than left blank. The compressed `sixteen_k` block was the next East Asia target because it made 316-439 northern China look like one long rectangle.
- Source grounding: Britannica describes the Sixteen Kingdoms as many short-lived Xiongnu, Jie, Xianbei, Di, Qiang, and related regimes after Western Jin collapse, and identifies Northern Wei as the durable northern unifier. Cambridge notes that the "Sixteen Kingdoms" label compresses a very complicated 304-439 field with more than sixteen significant states. Smithsonian's Period of Division summary supports Western Jin's 316 collapse, Eastern Jin in the south, and Northern Wei unifying the north in 439.
- Design decision: split the old northern block into seven owner-filled phases: `early_sixteen_kingdoms` (316-351), `former_qin_guanzhong` + `rival_north_kingdoms` (351-376), `former_qin_north_unified` (376-383), `post_fei_north_kingdoms` (383-386), and `northern_wei_rise` + `later_sixteen_kingdoms` (386-439).
- Design decision: use concrete owners where defensible and composite owners where precision would be false. Former Qin and Northern Wei receive named half-lane phases; the remaining courts are represented by `Rival Northern Kingdoms`, `Post-Fei River North`, and `Later 16 Kingdoms` rather than blank land or a false single state.
- Added descriptions, detail metadata, capitals, wiki mappings, relationship links, global events for 376 / 383 / 439, East Asia local events, and active assets `v210`.

- DOM geometry checks confirmed the new Tetris seams are closed: Former Qin/Rival split, Northern Wei/Later Sixteen split, and every vertical handoff from 316 through 439 measured 0px gap.
- Follow-up visual note: the 4th-century East Asia focus is now data-correct but dense when connection labels and global event markers are both on. A later pass should add local label avoidance or reduce label verbosity in dense focus bands.

## v211 Dense Label Collision Plan
- The v210 East Asia owner model was correct, but the 4th-century focus band exposed a separate reading problem: connection-label text and close global event markers could crowd around Former Qin, Fei River, Eastern Jin, and Northern Wei transitions.
- Design decision: keep the relationship graph intact. Collision avoidance should hide only the optional SVG text labels, not the arrows, paths, hover targets, or detail-panel relationships.
- Implemented a post-layout connection-label pruning pass. Each label group receives metadata for connection index, type, and distance; rendered bounding boxes are padded and scored so conquest, succession, and conflict labels survive before lower-priority or longer-distance labels.
- Implemented horizontal event-marker lanes on the global event rail. Close markers are assigned the first free lane, and the rail widens only as much as the current marker density requires.
- Active assets now load `styles.css?v=211`, `print.css?v=211`, and `app.js?v=211`.
- Verification passed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, active asset scan, and headless Chrome/CDP desktop + 390px Chinese mobile East Asia QA.

- Residual visual risk: event markers can still sit close to chart content on narrow mobile screens because the global rail overlays the timeline. A future pass should consider reserving a slim gutter or fading event markers while the user is focused inside dense chart content.

## v212 Northern/Southern Dynasties Split Plan
- User feedback accepted non-contiguous/split fragments when the simplified grid cannot show every real-world neighbor, but still objected to blank or generic territory. The next East Asia target was the post-439 Northern/Southern Dynasties row because it still compressed a complex century into broad northern and southern rectangles.
- Source grounding: Britannica's Six Dynasties overview gives the southern succession Liu-Song (420-479), Southern Qi (479-502), Southern Liang (502-557), Southern Chen (557-589), and the northern sequence Northern Wei (386-534/535), Eastern Wei (534-550), Western Wei (535-556/557), Northern Qi (550-577), and Northern Zhou (557-581). Britannica's China history page supports Northern Zhou reunifying the north in 577, Yang Jian founding Sui, and Sui conquering the last Jiankang dynasty in 589. Cambridge History chapter summaries support the Eastern Wei / Northern Qi and Western Wei / Northern Zhou paired successor structures after the Northern Wei split.
- Design decision: split the north into owner-conserving half-lanes. `eastern_wei` and `western_wei_bridge` begin at the 534 split; `western_wei` formalizes in 535; `northern_qi` replaces Eastern Wei in 550; `northern_zhou` replaces Western Wei in 557; `northern_zhou_unified` owns the full north from 577 to 581 before Sui.
- Design decision: split the south into named Jiankang owners. `liu_song_south`, `southern_qi`, `liang_dynasty`, and `chen_dynasty` replace the generic southern block; `sui_unified` has both a 589 succession from Sui core and a conquest edge from Chen.
- Updated descriptions, detail metadata, capitals, wiki mappings, relationship links, global/local events for 534 / 550 / 557 / 577 / 589, the Chinese-rule Vietnam remote-owner chain, and active assets to `v212`.

## v215 Early Caliphate Iraq / Persia Parallel-Lane Plan

The source story is provincial administration under one caliphate, not Iraq and Persia conquering pieces from each other.
- Design decision: remove the `taper-right` / `taper-left` shapes from `rashidun`, `rashidun_persia`, `umayyad_iraq`, and `umayyad_persia`. Rashidun Iraq still starts in 636 and Persia only appears after 651, so the eastern war is not backfilled; after 651 they are parallel same-caliphate regional lanes.
- Design decision: keep the direct same-color seam behavior. It makes the adjacent Iraq/Persia lanes read as a continuous political field while still allowing hover/click to distinguish the regional entries.

## v216 Roman Provincial Parallel-Lane Plan
- The post-v215 automatic-fill audit found 113 adjacent fills and 173 explicit fills. The clearest remaining same-polity pattern was Europe: Roman Republic/Empire/Late Roman provincial lanes for Greece/Balkans, Gaul, Hispania, and Britain were still drawn as if internal provinces occupied each other's missing strips.
- Source grounding: Britannica's Roman Britain page supports Britain as a Roman provincial field after Claudius; Britannica's Gallic Wars and Gaul pages support Caesar's conquest of Gaul and later Roman provincial organization; Britannica's Spain Romanization page supports Hispania as Roman provinces; Britannica's Roman Empire timeline supports Hadrianic consolidation and Diocletianic administrative reorganization. The source story is provincial administration inside one Roman state, not province-to-province land transfer.
- Design decision: remove shapes, explicit owner notches, and adjacent-fill plans from eleven same-state targets: `roman_republic_iberia`, `roman_republic_3`, `roman_republic_gaul`, `roman_empire_greece`, `roman_empire_gaul`, `roman_empire_hispania`, `roman_britain`, `roman_late_greece`, `roman_late_gaul`, `roman_late_hispania`, and `w_roman_gaul`.
- Design decision: preserve true non-internal cases. `roman_transalpine_gaul` and `celtic_gaul_late` still show the pre-Caesar frontier edge. `w_roman_hispania` still has a custom post-409 cutout explicitly filled by `hispania_successor_foederati`, because Suebi/Vandal/Alan/early Visigothic pressure is a named local successor field rather than a Roman internal province.
- Updated the Roman target descriptions and territory notes to say where the lane is a whole provincial unit and where a real successor strip remains. Active assets now load `v216`.
- Verification passed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, active asset scan, VM audit with 8 regions, 829 entities, 743 connections, automatic adjacent fills reduced from 113 to 105, explicit fills reduced from 173 to 170, and no duplicate IDs, missing endpoints, unknown categories, or v216 target fill rows.

## v222 Central Asia Transoxiana / Sogdian-Oasis Enrichment Plan
- Started from a fresh VM union-coverage audit of the current v221 dataset. The largest remaining ownerless-looking band is Central Asia `slot 0-2` from AD 465 to 740, covering the simplified Transoxiana / Turkmenistan / Margiana side between Kidarite Bactria and the caliphal lane.
- Source grounding: Encyclopaedia Iranica's Sogdiana history article supports 5th-7th century Sogdian urban growth, the Hephthalite partition around 560, Sogdiana passing under Turkic / Western Turkic / On Ok / Turgesh control for roughly a century and a half, independent city-principalities around Samarkand, Panjikent, Bukhara, Kish, and Chach, and the systematic Arab conquest from 705 with Samarkand falling in 712. Iranica's Khorasan article supports the unstable early Muslim frontier, local magnates seeking help from Hephthalites, Western Turks / Turgesh, and Chinese claims, and a repeated capture-rebellion-recapture pattern. Britannica's Qutaybah ibn Muslim page supports Bukhara 706-709, Samarkand 710-712, Khwarezm, and nominal Arab rule farther north by 715.
- Design decision: do not widen `hephthalite`, `gokturk`, or `umayyad_ca` into the whole gap. The more honest compressed lane is a three-stage owner chain: `hephthalite_transoxiana` (465-560), `sogdian_turkic_oases` (560-705), and `arab_sogdian_contest` (705-740).
- Design decision: `sogdian_turkic_oases` and `arab_sogdian_contest` are composite/confederational owner layers, not clean bounded states. Their purpose is to keep Sogdian cities, Western Turkic / Turgesh suzerainty, Qutayba-era conquest, tribute, garrisons, and resistance visible without fabricating one uniform imperial owner.

## v225 Southeast Asia Malayu / Dharmasraya Enrichment Plan

## v226 Central Asia Rouran-Gaoche Steppe Enrichment Plan
- Started from a corrected VM interval audit of Central Asia after v225. The old ranked row under-reported the lower boundary: the actual northern-steppe half-lane gap is `slot 2-2.5` from AD 430 to 552, beginning when `kangju` ends and closing when `gokturk` starts.
- Source grounding: University of Washington Silk Road notes place Kangju's heartland along the middle Syr Darya and distinguish it from Sogdiana; Britannica places the Rouran/Juan-juan empire in the late fourth to mid-sixth-century Central Asian steppe sequence and records its destruction by the Turks in 552; Encyclopaedia Iranica keeps the Hephthalite core in Bactria/Tokharistan and explains the Turk-Sasanian defeat of Hephthalite power in 558-561; the Rouran chronology source records western reach toward Xinjiang, Ili, Balkhash, Gaoche/Tiele pressure, and Bumin's pre-552 steppe consolidation.
