## v229 Visual / Layout Correction Plan
- Started from the latest user critique, not a new source-enrichment target: same-color adjacency should hide borders visually without implying that separate detail records are merged; dark mode should use darker harmonious map fills with light labels; Taiwan should not sit visually on the Beijing-core side; remaining blanks should stay visible as honest data-refinement work.
- Design decision: all rendered polity blocks get a seam group keyed by explicit same-polity grouping when available, otherwise by entity ID. Territory fill pieces inherit their owner ID/group, owner color, and owner region so cutout fragments can visually merge with the corresponding owner block while unrelated same-color neighbors remain separated.
- Design decision: East Asia render-only order becomes `3, 4, 2, 0, 7, 8, 5, 6`, reading west/north interiors, Mongolia, Northeast, China core, Vietnam / South China Sea, Taiwan, Korea, Japan. Raw data slots remain unchanged.
- Design decision: dark mode now computes inline block fills through a dark-tint function and rerenders the timeline when the mode changes, because the old CSS-only toggle could not adjust inline background colors.
- Implementation note: explicit cutout blocks use the full raw slot span rather than the ordinary compressed width. This keeps owner-fill pieces aligned to adjacent slot boundaries, which is necessary for Golden Horde / Timurid-style fills to merge visually without background slivers.
- Verification passed: static checks, VM data audit, active asset scan, desktop Playwright East Asia/Taiwan layout check, Central Asia Golden Horde seam check, and 390px Chinese dark-mode check. Remaining blank-lane work is unchanged and should continue from the post-v228 ranked gap queue.

## v239 Southeast Asia Pyu / Pagan Handoff Refinement Plan
- Fresh post-v238 context ranked Southeast Asia `slot 4-5` from AD 840 to 849 as the largest remaining real blank-looking band. Code inspection shows the band is the Myanmar / Irrawaddy lane between `pyu` ending at AD 840 and `pagan` starting at AD 849.
- Source direction: Britannica places Nanzhao raids and the fall of the Pyu capital Halingyi before the Burmans established Pagan as their capital city in 849; UNESCO places Pyu Ancient Cities in a long 200 BC-AD 900 urban tradition; EBSCO places Nanzhao's subjugation of Pyu in 832 and links the disruption to Pagan's later rise.
- Modeling decision: extend `pyu` to AD 849 and add explicit Nanzhao/Pagan handoff context rather than creating a tiny separate nine-year polity or backdating mature 11th-century Pagan power.
- Implementation completed: updated `pyu` and `pagan` descriptions/details, moved `pyu.end` from 840 to 849, added the `pagan -> pyu` succession relationship, added 832/849 Southeast Asia regional markers and a global 849 Pagan event, updated README / next-prompt / findings notes, and active assets `v239`.

## v254 Latest User-Review Correction Plan
- User clarification: same-color seams are not semantic polity merging. Adjacent blocks/fill pieces with the same rendered source color should hide their shared border as a visual affordance only; hover, focus, click targets, detail records, relationships, and IDs remain separate.
- v254 seam decision: `applySameColorSeams()` now groups rendered pieces by `region|color`, not `region|color|seamGroup`. The `seamGroup` field can still document data intent, but it is no longer required to hide a same-color internal border.
- v254 interaction decision: same-color seam sides are transparent at rest, but hover/focus restores the local outline so users can see and inspect individual neighboring blocks.
- v254 dark-mode decision: dark territory fills are further desaturated/darkened (`darkTint` source mix 0.16 / saturation mix 0.46), and dark-mode block labels are explicitly light (`#F6F0E8`).
- v254 East Asia layout decision: raw Taiwan records remain `slot 8`, but the render-only East Asia guide now orders China core -> Taiwan -> Vietnam -> Korea -> Japan, so Ming Zheng / Tungning is next to the China-coast guide without becoming a Beijing-core fill.
- Verification completed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, asset scan (`v254`), source layout audit, DOM dark-mode color audit, desktop and mobile headless Chrome/CDP QA, and hover seam QA. Results: all active resources load `v254`, dark-mode max sampled block luminance is 45.34 with no white/transparent blocks, sampled label luminance is about 240.7, `tungning` renders raw slot 8 / layout slot 5 while Japan is layout slot 8, `golden_horde` and its fill pieces carry same-color seam classes, 390px mobile has no horizontal overflow, and no upside-down Chinese transforms were found.
- Verification error log: the first CDP verifier failed because Node could not infer module format with `require()` plus top-level `await`; rerun with an async wrapper. The second failed because `Target.createTarget` rejected window sizing parameters; rerun with target creation plus `Emulation.setDeviceMetricsOverride`.
- Screenshot inspected: `/tmp/history_visual_v254_dark_1722.png`.

## v256-v257 Influence Cutout Cleanup Plan
- Starting observation: the v255 delegated audit found no large blank blocks and could not reproduce the old Ming Zheng / Beijing-core placement, but it ranked the Americas preclassic Mesoamerican influence-fill cluster as a high semantic risk. A follow-up read-only review also flagged `khmer_thai` as the same pattern: an influence/frontier strip using automatic adjacent cutout ownership.
- Source direction: Olmec, Maya Preclassic, Zapotec / Monte Alban, and broader Preclassic Mesoamerica should read as interacting regional cultural fields, not as one another's territorial cutout owners. Khmer / Lopburi authority in the Chao Phraya / Thai basin before Sukhothai is historically visible, but its connection to Angkor should be shown as a whole frontier strip plus relationships rather than as a missing bite filled by Angkor core.
- Modeling decision: remove `shape`, `notches`, and automatic adjacent-fill behavior from `olmec_maya_influence`, `early_maya_formative`, `maya_preclassic`, `preclassic`, `zapotec_preclassic`, and `khmer_thai`. Preserve separate hover/detail records, categories, relationship context, and same-color seam hiding.

- Verification completed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, active asset scan (`v257`), CDP detail-panel QA for Americas and Southeast Asia targets, full all-region desktop/mobile dark-mode regression, event-rail regression, Taiwan slot regression, and data integrity / coverage audit. ## v258 Same-Color / Dark-Mode / Taiwan-Strait Visual Plan
- Starting observation: the latest user review clarified again that same-color blocks should not be semantically merged; they should simply hide shared borders. Code and browser QA showed dark-mode hover/focus could still redraw same-color seam sides, and the China-core / Taiwan render placement looked too attached even though Taiwan data remained raw `slot 8`.
- Coverage decision: do not add new historical blocks in this pass. A fresh union-coverage audit found no gaps at the current two-year / 0.24-slot threshold, and an AD 1722 point audit found no ownerless visible lane segments. The remaining blank perception is visual: light fills were too pale, single-year boundary artifacts remain below the data-fill threshold, and island lanes needed better separation.
- Visual decision: keep same-color seams transparent even on hover/focus; preserve separate hover/detail/focus targets through interaction state and tooltips rather than redrawing the internal border. Slightly deepen both light-mode and dark-mode fills while keeping dark-mode labels light.
- Layout decision: add a narrow render-only East Asia gap after the China-core source group. This gap acts as a strait/island separator before Taiwan while leaving Ming Zheng / Tungning, Qing Taiwan, Japanese Taiwan, and ROC Taiwan in raw `slot 8` and avoiding any old `qing_beijing -> tungning` cutout.
- Implementation completed: added `gapsAfterSourceEnd` support to the region layout guide, rendered `.layout-gap` strips, updated East Asia's guide, adjusted `paleTint()` and `darkTint()`, removed same-color seam hover/focus re-outline rules, updated README / findings / progress notes, and bumped active assets to `v258`.
- Verification completed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, active asset scan (`v258`), desktop and mobile CDP QA, hover seam QA, light/dark luminance scans, coverage audits, and screenshot inspection. Results: Golden Horde seam sides remain transparent after hover, Taiwan has a 19px strait gap from Qing China while remaining closer than Japan, no large coverage gaps or AD 1722 ownerless lanes, no whiteish light/dark sampled blocks, no upside-down Chinese transforms, no horizontal overflow, and dense event markers still have 0 overlaps.

## v260 Jomon / Yayoi Contact-Cutout Cleanup Plan
- Starting observation: `jomon` and `yayoi` text already said Korean-peninsula contact / transmission, not political absorption, yet the blocks still used Korean entities as cutout owners. This makes cultural contact look like territorial ownership.
- Source direction: Britannica and the Met support Jomon as an archipelago culture with peninsula commerce/contact, and Yayoi as a Japan-side transformation involving rice agriculture, metallurgy, Korean/continental routes, pottery/burial parallels, and population admixture rather than a Korean territorial annexation of Japan.
- Modeling decision: keep Jomon and Yayoi as whole Japanese archipelago cultural lanes; use relationship links and detail text for contact, trade, rice, metallurgy, and continental influence. Preserve `jomon -> korea_prehistoric`, add `yayoi -> gojoseon`, and keep the existing Jomon -> Yayoi -> Kofun succession chain.

The new Yayoi route exists in data/detail; its canvas label can be collision-pruned at dense zoom while the path and detail relationship remain available.

## v261 Toungoo / Ayutthaya Suzerainty-Cutout Cleanup Plan
- Starting observation: `toungoo_siam` and `ayutthaya_vassal` are already described as short-lived Burmese suzerainty / vassalage records after Bayinnaung's 1569 capture, but reciprocal taper geometry still makes the relationship read like two territorial pieces owning each other's cut edge.
- Source direction: Britannica supports Bayinnaung's conquest of Ayutthaya, installation of a vassal, more than 15 years of Myanmar dominance, and Naresuan's 1584 renunciation of vassalage. Journal of the Siam Society material supports the military-route and siege context. Together they justify separate records plus relationships, not cutout-owner geometry.
- Modeling decision: keep two separate 1569-1584 half-lane records so Burmese suzerainty and Ayutthaya court continuity are both visible; remove `shape` / cutout behavior from both; add explicit relationship links for the 1569 conquest from independent Ayutthaya and the 1584 Naresuan break into restored Ayutthaya.
- Verification target: active assets `v261`; `toungoo_siam` and `ayutthaya_vassal` have no shape plan, no `clip-path`, and 0 target owner-fill rows; detail panels show `疆域语义` but no `缺口承接`; all-region desktop/mobile dark-mode regressions still pass, including no white blocks, no upside-down Chinese, no horizontal overflow, and preserved Taiwan / same-color seam behavior.
- v261 verification finding before closure: target geometry was clean, but `toungoo_siam` detail still showed `缺口承接` because `cambodia_post` used it as a full-period Siam-facing cutout owner. Treat this as a failed semantic regression and continue into v262.

## v262 Post-Angkor Cambodia Pressure-Geometry Cleanup Plan
- Starting observation: `cambodia_post`'s old full-height right-edge cutout used Ayutthaya, Toungoo Siam, restored Ayutthaya, Thonburi, and Rattanakosin to represent pressure/vassalage from 1431 to 1863. Browser QA proved that this polluted Toungoo Siam's detail panel and overstated pressure as owner geometry.
- Source direction: Britannica supports long Cambodia weakness, Siam/Vietnam protection politics, and lost territory/sovereignty, but the concrete territorial loss in this period is the 1794 Siamese appropriation of Battambang and Siem Reap until 1907. AAS supports early-19th-century tributary status to both Siam and Vietnam plus the 1863 French protectorate.
- Modeling decision: keep Post-Angkor Cambodia mostly whole; carry broad Siamese/Vietnamese pressure by text and relationships; retain only a 1794-1863 Rattanakosin owner fill for the western provinces; add the 1794 relationship link.
- Verification target: active assets `v262`; `toungoo_siam` and `ayutthaya_vassal` detail panels have no `缺口承接` / `Cutout Owners`; `cambodia_post` has exactly one source fill owned by `rattanakosin` for the 1794-1863 western loss; desktop/mobile dark-mode regressions still pass.

## v264 Akkad / Elam Pressure-Cutout Cleanup Plan

## v269 South Asia Harappan Fringe-Cutout Cleanup Plan

## v271 BMAC / Oxus Steppe-Contact Cutout Cleanup Plan
- Fresh post-v270 semantic-risk audit ranked `bmac` as a high-risk remaining case: it is a Bronze Age oasis / archaeological network record, but still used `shape: 'taper-right'`, making northern steppe cultures appear to fill a missing piece of the BMAC lane.
- Source direction: the British Museum describes BMAC / Oxus Civilization as a modern archaeological designation for a Bronze Age culture along the upper Amu Darya in present-day Turkmenistan, Afghanistan, southern Uzbekistan, and western Tajikistan, with possible extensions and long-distance trade/production uses for seals; the Met describes Bactria-Margiana as a highly developed late third / early second millennium BCE western Central Asian civilization with contacts to Iran. These sources support a whole oasis-cultural lane linked by exchange, not grassland ownership of an oasis cutout.
- Modeling decision: keep `bmac` and `kazakh_bronze` as adjacent whole cultural lanes. Remove BMAC's land-bite geometry; keep Oxus-Afghan, mountain-oasis, and steppe-oasis contact semantics through existing relationship links and details.

- Source direction: British Museum, Smithsonian, and Encyclopaedia Iranica material all support Sogdiana as an oasis / agricultural corridor around Zarafshan and Kashka-Darya / Samarkand-Bukhara contexts, while steppe / Saka pressure is an adjacency and frontier-contact problem rather than an oasis cutout.
- Modeling decision: keep `sogdiana_early` as a whole Zarafshan / Kashka-Darya lane beside the late Bronze steppe and Saka / Scythian lane. Carry steppe-oasis contact through relationship labels and territory/detail text instead of `Cutout Owners`.

Verification is next.
- Wording polish completed: v284 keeps the same geometry and relationships, but replaces user-facing "cutout owner" wording in Early Sogdiana / Steppe Cultures / Scythians details with plain adjacency and no-land-bite language. Active assets now load `v284`.

## v289 Central Asia Auto-Fill Tightening Plan
- Starting observation: the latest false-fill audit found that the automatic adjacent-fill fallback was still too permissive. A neighbor with only partial time overlap could be treated as the owner of a full default taper notch, creating a visual land-bite claim that the data did not support.
- Source direction: Transoxiana / Khorasan / steppe-frontier histories around Abbasid, Qara-Khanid, Seljuq, and Timurid Central Asia are better represented as oasis, route, Khorasan, and steppe-adjacent lanes with relationship links unless the receiving owner covers the missing interval. The partial-overlap cases should not become automatic owner fills.
- Modeling decision: keep automatic owner fills only for nearly complete adjacent coverage. If the best adjacent candidate does not cover at least 98% of the missing time window, do not render the fill. Use frontier or political relationships for the remaining Central Asia adjacency semantics.
- Implementation completed: replaced the permissive adjacent owner lookup with `buildAdjacentNotchFill()`, which checks overlap share and snaps only tiny edge gaps; removed shape geometry from `abbasid_ca`, `qara_khanid`, `seljuk_ca`, `seljuk_ca_south`, and `timurid_south`; rewrote bilingual descriptions and territory notes; added five Central Asia frontier/political relationships; updated README / findings / progress / next-prompt notes; and bumped active assets to `v289`.

## v299 Cross-Region Automatic-Fill Cleanup Plan
- Starting observation: the post-v298 shape audit still ranked several cross-region adjacency cases as high-risk false-fill readings. Mughal Deccan, Delhi Deccan / Pandya, Umayyad Ifriqiya / Nubia, and Ayutthaya / late Sukhothai were visually describable as neighboring campaign, pressure, route, or absorption records, but old taper/hourglass geometry could still imply a literal owner-filled land bite.
- Source direction: Britannica's Aurangzeb and Delhi Sultanate / Khalji / Tughluq material supports Deccan campaigns, raids, tribute, annexation, and later Maratha resistance as political-military relationships. Britannica's Sukhothai / Ayutthaya material supports Thai consolidation and Sukhothai absorption by Ayutthaya without reciprocal clipped land geometry. Britannica and UChicago Nubia material support Christian Nubia as a separate middle-Nile lane while Ifriqiya / the Maghreb belong to the North African conquest route after Carthage.
- Modeling decision: keep the six target records whole. Represent conquest routes, raids, absorption, imperial-core pairing, and resistance through relationship links and territory/detail text; do not let neighboring lanes become automatic notch owners for these cases.
- Implementation completed: removed shape geometry from `mughal_deccan`, `delhi_deccan`, `pandya`, `umayyad_africa`, `ayutthaya_rise`, and `sukhothai_late`; rewrote bilingual descriptions, details, and territory notes away from owner-fill language; added four relationship links for Egypt-to-Ifriqiya, Khalji raids into Tamil south, Mughal Deccan/core pairing, and Maratha resistance; and bumped active assets to `v299`.
- Verification completed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, VM data/shape/gap audit, and headless Chrome desktop/mobile dark-mode QA passed. Results: 924 entities / 1012 relationships / 176 events; 0 duplicate IDs, missing endpoints, bad connection types, bad categories, or corrected real-slot gaps over 1 year; rendered shape plans dropped to 76 and fill pieces to 104; all six v299 target records have no raw shape, raw notches, shape plan, or fill rows; all-region v299 dark mode renders 924 blocks / 104 fills / 176 events / 1012 connection paths, with no pale or transparent blocks, no low-contrast labels, no upside-down Chinese, no non-micro blank-text blocks, and no document overflow. Ming Zheng / Qing Taiwan remain raw Taiwan `slot 8` at render layout slot 5.95 between Qing south-coast China and Edo Japan.

## v300 Late Khmer / Tai-Polity False-Fill Cleanup Plan
- Starting observation: after v299, `khmer_late` remained one visible residual from the older v164 Southeast Asia owner-fill model. It still used a full-height right-edge notch whose owners were `sukhothai` and `ayutthaya_rise`, even though v299 had already made the adjacent Thai transition records whole and relationship-based.
- Source direction: Britannica supports Sukhothai as a Tai revolt / breakaway from Khmer authority in the upper Chao Phraya basin, Ayutthaya as the longer-lived Chao Phraya successor and Tai consolidation center, and the 1431 Tai/Ayutthaya sack of Angkor as the end point of the Khmer empire. This supports pressure, breakaway, and conquest relationships, not a continuing Tai-owned cutout inside the Angkor/Cambodian lane.
- Modeling decision: keep `khmer_late` as a whole reduced Angkor / Cambodian core lane beside the Thai basin. Carry Sukhothai breakaway, Ayutthaya pressure, and the sack of Angkor through explicit relationship links and detail text.
- Implementation completed: removed `khmer_late` notches, rewrote bilingual description/detail/territory wording away from Tai cutout-owner language, added `sukhothai -> khmer_late` for the breakaway and `ayutthaya_rise -> khmer_late` for the 1431 sack of Angkor, and bumped active assets to `v300`.
- First browser QA result: static checks and all-region dark-mode QA passed for v300, but the high-zoom Southeast Asia target QA showed `素可泰脱离高棉权威` being pruned by connection-label collision logic behind a same-year succession label. This was a real readability regression for the relationship-based model, so v300 is superseded by v301 for the final verified artifact.

## v301 Late Khmer Breakaway Label Priority Plan
- Starting observation: after removing the false Tai-owned cutout from `khmer_late`, the relationship label carrying the Sukhothai breakaway semantics must remain visible in the target QA view. Type-only label scoring preferred `succession` over `political`, which hid the key explanatory label.
- Modeling decision: keep the blocks and relationships unchanged, but add a narrow optional label-priority boost for selected relationships. This preserves collision pruning generally while allowing historically explanatory labels to survive when they would otherwise be hidden by a same-year label.
- Implementation completed: added `labelPriority` support in `scoreConnectionLabel()`, set the Sukhothai-to-Late-Khmer breakaway link to `labelPriority: 40`, and bumped active assets to `v301`.
- Verification completed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, active asset scan, VM data/shape/gap audit, desktop and 390px mobile all-region Chinese dark-mode QA, and Southeast Asia AD 1431 Chinese dark-mode target QA passed. Results: 924 entities / 1014 relationships / 176 events; rendered shape plans remain 75 and fill pieces 102; corrected coverage has 98 one-year seams and 0 gaps over 1 year; all four Late Khmer / Tai target records have no raw shape, no shape plan, no source/owner fill rows, and `clip-path: none`; v301 browser QA renders 924 blocks / 102 fills / 176 events / 1014 paths with no pale or transparent dark blocks, low-contrast labels, upside-down Chinese, non-micro blank-text blocks, dense event text overflow, label-overflow rows, or document overflow. Southeast Asia AD 1431 shows the visible labels `素可泰脱离高棉权威`, `阿瑜陀耶攻陷吴哥`, and `素可泰并入阿瑜陀耶`.

## v302 Chinese-Rule Vietnam Remote-Fill Cleanup Plan
- Starting observation: a fresh post-v301 rendered-shape audit found `chinese_vn` as the highest remaining geometry risk. It rendered one full-height remote-owner cutout and 15 owner-fill pieces for mainland Chinese dynasties. That preserved detail but made the already named `Chinese Rule` / `北属时期` block look like a missing-land polygon rather than a whole Red River commandery/protectorate administration lane.
- Source direction: Britannica supports Han conquest / annexation in 111 BCE, military districts and later direct Chinese administration in the Red River delta, Tang-era Chinese rule until Tang decline, uprisings leading to independence in 939, and later Ly consolidation. This supports whole foreign-administration lane semantics with relationship/detail links, not 15 remote owner-fill fragments.
- Modeling decision: keep `chinese_vn` whole. Represent the Han commanderies, Tang Annan Protectorate, Southern Han / Lingnan context, and Bach Dang independence through relationship links and detail text. Do not restore `notches`, `shape`, or remote `notchOwners` for Han/Wu/Jin/Southern-Dynasties/Sui/Tang/Southern-Han owners.
- Implementation completed: removed `chinese_vn` notches, rewrote bilingual description/detail/territory wording away from remote cutout-owner language, added `汉设交趾郡县`, `唐安南都护府`, and `独立前南汉控制交趾` relationship links with label priorities, updated README / next-prompt / planning notes, and bumped active assets to `v302`.
- Verification completed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, active asset scan, VM data/shape/gap audit, corrected real-slot-boundary coverage audit, East Asia AD 679 target browser QA, and all-region AD 1722 desktop / 390px mobile dark-mode QA passed. Results: 924 entities / 1017 relationships / 176 events; rendered shape plans dropped to 74 and rendered fill pieces to 87; `chinese_vn` has no raw shape, no notches, no shape plan, and 0 source/owner fill rows; corrected coverage has 98 one-year seams and 0 gaps over 1 year; v302 browser QA renders 924 blocks / 87 fills / 176 event markers / 1017 paths with no pale or transparent dark blocks, low-contrast labels, upside-down Chinese, non-micro blank blocks, dense event text overflow, label-overflow-hidden rows, console issues, or document overflow. Ming Zheng / Qing Taiwan remain raw Taiwan `slot 8` / layout slot `5.95`, with about 53px from Qing south-coast China and 131px before Edo Japan.

## v303 Visual Semantics, Dark Palette, Tiny Labels, and Saffarid/Samanid Cleanup Plan
- Starting observation: the latest review clarified that same-color adjacent blocks should stay separate records while hiding normal internal borders; dark-mode territory colors were still too pale; a few narrow blocks still looked blank; and Ming Zheng / Tungning Taiwan could still read too close to the Beijing/core mainland group rather than as an offshore lane.
- Source direction: Britannica supports Saffarids and Samanids as eastern Iranian / Khorasan-centered powers whose Abbasid relationship is recognition or caliphal context, not a Baghdad-owned cutout inside their lanes.
- Modeling decision: keep seam hiding visual-only. Use optional `seamGroup` only as an explicit render seam key for split same-polity pieces such as Golden Horde / Jochid or Chagatai / Timurid companion records; do not merge IDs, hover targets, detail panels, or relationship data. Keep Saffarid and Samanid Iran whole and express Abbasid context with relationships, not land-bite geometry.
- Implementation completed: added optional render-only `data-seam-group` support with color/region fallback, set explicit seam groups for Golden Horde, Chagatai, and Timurid companion records, darkened `darkTint()`, strengthened light/dark layout-gap styling, moved the East Asia render guide so Vietnam / South China Sea precedes Taiwan and Taiwan remains before Japan, removed Saffarid / Samanid Abbasid-context cutouts, added Abbasid-context relationships, lowered tiny-label thresholds, and bumped active assets to `v303`.
- Verification completed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, active asset scan, VM data/shape/gap audit, corrected true-slot coverage audit, all-region AD 1722 desktop dark/light browser QA, 390px mobile dark browser QA, and Middle East AD 903 target QA passed. Results: 924 entities / 1019 relationships / 176 events; rendered shape plans dropped to 72 and fill pieces to 85; corrected coverage has 17 one-year seams and 0 gaps over 1 year; all-region v303 QA renders 924 blocks / 85 fills / 176 event markers / 1019 paths with no pale/transparent blocks, low-contrast labels, upside-down Chinese, non-micro blank blocks, hidden labels, seam problems, or document overflow. Saffarid / Samanid targets have no raw shape, no notches, no shape plan, and 0 source/owner fill rows. Ming Zheng / Qing Taiwan render after Vietnam / South China Sea and before Edo Japan, with Qing Beijing core left of the China south-coast and Taiwan island lanes.

## v304 Same-Polity Cutout Cleanup and Readability Plan
- Starting observation: the latest user review clarified that same-color blocks are not semantically merged; the internal line should be hidden only when adjacent records share the rendered color. A fresh audit found two remaining same-polity / same-color cutouts that still contradicted that rule: `safavid` carved out `safavid_iraq`, and `qing` carved out `qing_manchuria`. Two stale no-plan shape fields also remained on `qing_south_campaigns` and `qing_manchuria`.
- Source direction: Britannica supports Qing as a Manchu regime established in Manchuria in 1636 and ruling China after 1644, which fits separate Manchuria and China-proper lanes connected by relationships. Britannica also supports Safavid Iran plus short Safavid Baghdad/Iraq control before the 1534 Ottoman capture, which fits a paired same-empire Iraq lane rather than a west-edge bite inside the Iranian core.
- Modeling decision: keep `qing`, `qing_manchuria`, `qing_south_campaigns`, `safavid`, and `safavid_iraq` as separate records for hover/detail/search, but do not render land-bite geometry between same-polity fragments. Carry the pairings through `qing_manchuria -> qing` and `safavid_iraq -> safavid` political relationships while normal same-color seam hiding removes the visible border.
- Implementation completed: removed the Safavid Iran notch and Qing China-proper taper/notch owner fields; removed stale `shape: 'taper-left'` from `qing_south_campaigns` and `qing_manchuria`; rewrote bilingual descriptions/details/territory notes away from cutout-owner wording; added the two pairing relationships; added dynamic per-block text color so light-mode dark tinted blocks use light text; and bumped active assets to `v304`.
- Verification completed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, VM data/shape audit, corrected true-slot coverage audit, and headless Chrome desktop dark/light, mobile dark, and Middle East AD 1534 target QA passed. Results: 924 entities / 1021 relationships / 176 events; rendered shape plans dropped to 70 and fill pieces to 83; corrected coverage has 0 gaps over 1 year; desktop/mobile all-region v304 QA renders 924 blocks / 83 fills / 176 event markers / 1021 paths with no pale/transparent dark blocks, low-contrast labels, upside-down Chinese, non-micro blank blocks, hidden labels, label overflow, or target clip paths. Qing / Manchuria / Qing south coast and Safavid / Safavid Iraq have `clip-path: none` and same-color seam classes; Qing Taiwan remains after Vietnam / South China Sea and before Edo Japan.

## v305 Column / Region Layout Optimization Plan
- Starting observation: the rendered all-region order still came from `CONFIG.visibleRegions` object insertion order, placing Southeast Asia after the Americas even though the toolbar and historical relationship model treat Southeast Asia as closely related to East Asia and South Asia.
- Modeling decision: make the global region order explicit as East Asia -> Southeast Asia -> South Asia -> Central Asia -> Middle East -> Europe -> Africa -> Americas. Keep this as display order only; URL parsing, visibility state, data keys, and raw historical slots remain unchanged.
- Lane-guide decision: keep the existing render-only lane-group optimizer, but update East Asia and add guides for Southeast Asia and South Asia. The guides keep cross-slot groups intact, then place related lanes nearer: East Asia moves Taiwan near China core while putting Vietnam on the Southeast Asia-facing edge; Southeast Asia begins with Vietnam/Champa and mainland lanes; South Asia puts maritime/eastern lanes toward Southeast Asia and Punjab/NW toward Central Asia.
- Implementation completed: added `REGION_DISPLAY_ORDER`, routed visible-region rendering / legend / Compare options / share URL region serialization through it, updated `REGION_LAYOUT_GUIDES`, bumped active assets to `v305`, and updated README.
- Verification completed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, active asset scan, VM data/layout audit, and headless Chrome desktop/mobile QA passed. Results: 924 entities / 1021 relationships / 176 rendered event markers; 0 duplicate IDs, missing endpoints, bad categories, bad connection types, layout mapping errors, console/log issues, body overflow, or label-overflow-hidden blocks. Browser QA confirmed desktop/mobile region headers and Compare options use East Asia -> Southeast Asia -> South Asia -> Central Asia -> Middle East -> Europe -> Africa -> Americas, and key East Asia / Southeast Asia / South Asia blocks render in the intended layout-slot order.

## v306 Event / Connection Regression and Modern Color Audit Plan
- Starting observation: the user-reported all-region `zoom=2&year=1895&x=0.0351` URL still rendered all 176 events and 1021 connection paths, but events were forced into dense micro-dot mode because density only checked total event count, and connection labels were pruned from 1021 candidates to 594 visible labels. Modern Mongolia also used the same source color as PRC China proper, allowing a false same-color seam reading.
- Implementation completed: changed dense event rail selection to depend on average event pixel spacing, added vertical offset candidates for high-zoom connection labels before pruning, changed `mongolia_mod` to an independent green, confirmed `roc_taiwan` already matches `roc_postwar` / ROC mainland color, changed `levant_modern` away from Saudi Arabia's modern green, and bumped active assets to `v306`.
- Verification completed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, active asset scan, exact-URL headless Chrome QA, mobile/desktop all-region QA, modern same-color adjacency filtering, and runtime data integrity audit passed. Results: exact v306 URL loads `styles.css?v=306`, `print.css?v=306`, and `app.js?v=306`; renders 924 blocks / 176 event markers / 1021 paths / 893 connection labels with 128 labels pruned after nudging; event rail is not dense at `zoom=2`; all data audits report 0 duplicate IDs, missing endpoints, bad categories, bad dates, bad slots, bad connection types, bad event regions, invalid event dates, or unrendered connections.

## v307 Bottom-Layering Regression Plan
- Starting observation: the reported bottom view still had all event and connection DOM nodes, but screenshot and `elementFromPoint` checks showed most bottom markers/labels were underneath dynasty block content. The lower-right collapsed legend also covered a visible piece of the timeline. The chronicle footer was below the viewport, so it was not the covering element.
- Implementation completed: raised `.connection-line` SVGs and their inline render layer above dynasty blocks, added a high `z-index` to `.global-events-track`, compressed `.legend.collapsed` to a 34px icon-only fixed control, and bumped active assets to `v307`.
- Verification completed: `node --check app.js` and `git diff --check` passed. The Browser plugin rejected post-fix screenshot capture for the `file://` URL under its URL policy, so final visual re-screenshot through that tool is deferred until the page is served through an allowed URL or opened manually.

## v308 Overview Display Consistency Plan
- Starting observation: at `zoom=0.1`, `linkLabels=1` still produced no connection text because label creation was hard-gated on `CONFIG.yearHeight > 1.0`; global event markers were positioned inside the horizontal timeline wrapper, so they appeared tied to a region instead of the viewport; and East Asia had internal island / coast gaps while major region boundaries such as Europe / Africa / Americas only had a one-pixel separator.
- Implementation completed: removed the zoom gate from connection-label creation and kept collision pruning as the readability control, with smaller low-zoom label text. Converted the global event rail to a fixed viewport-right layer and added scroll/resize position recomputation based on each marker's content Y. Added render-only region-boundary gaps after visible regions, without changing raw entity slots or data semantics, and made region toggles rebuild the global event rail.
- Verification completed: `node --check app.js` and `git diff --check` passed. Active assets are `v308`; visual screenshot verification is still limited by the in-app Browser `file://` URL policy.

## v311 Internal Geography Gaps and Event-Rail Interaction Plan
- Starting observation: major-region gaps were not enough. The same visual rule should apply inside regions where the simplified slots mix islands or separate continental landmasses: Europe needed Britain separated from neighboring mainland lanes, and the Americas needed Mesoamerica/Central America, South America, North America, and the Caribbean to read as distinct land/island systems. The dense event rail also needed an interaction model instead of simply stacking many dots on the right.
- Implementation completed: added `preserveOrder` layout guides so Europe and the Americas keep their existing slot order while gaining internal render-only gaps; Britain now has water gaps on both sides, and the Americas now has gaps after Central America, South America, and North America/Canada. The dense event rail now defaults to a compact edge stack, expands on hover/focus/click, shows numbers across the expanded stack, and shows a single event label beside the active dot. Markers hidden under the sticky header are removed from the interactive hit path.
- Verification completed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, and localhost Chrome screenshot QA passed. The checked URL loaded `v311` assets, rendered 267 overview connection labels after pruning, kept the dense event rail at 80px by default, expanded it to 404px on hover, and showed generated screenshots at `/tmp/history-visual-v311-default.png` and `/tmp/history-visual-v311-hover.png`.

## v312 Default Settings Plan
- Starting observation: the requested baseline should be Chinese UI with connection arrows visible but their text labels hidden. This should affect only no-parameter defaults; explicit URL flags such as `lang=en` or `linkLabels=1` must still override the defaults.
- Implementation completed: changed the app defaults to `language: 'cn'` and `showConnectionLabels: false`, updated initial HTML language/button/checkbox state, and bumped active assets to `v312`.
- Verification completed: `node --check app.js`, `git diff --check`, and no-parameter localhost Chrome QA passed. The browser loaded `v312` assets, showed Chinese UI text, left the Labels checkbox unchecked, rendered 1021 connection paths, and rendered 0 connection-label nodes.
